Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galiens tells us of a cure by which some were cured of pain in the groin and sciatic vein, and he recounts that they did nothing else, and that they were healed at one time when they had performed this cure, and he bathed as he is taught afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he adds in part that you take two pounds of fresh and dry green barley and grind it with some fat, and put on the groin and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours until the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter or bathe until the limb is slightly swollen, and then make him enter or lie down, and the pain will go away and be healed
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And such soaks must not be used with such medicines, except after the evacuation of bones.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And thus it is said that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with the tip of a needle, if there is any moisture there; it must be done in small parts.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and soak it in much oil, and put it on the pit which is between the thumb and the little finger, and the one which is called the fossicle
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dry needles and heating them until they are charred, and then putting them on the lint, and letting it stay there until it is stained; and doing this again and again until you think by feeling that it has gone down to the hip, and the pain has ceased; this manner of cautery is called "needle cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	Albucasim saith that our physicians often use this cautery because of its fearsome aftereffects, and those who have used it; and indeed all of them are scarred bones, which can suffer from it and leave their mark.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from sitting, or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar spreading of cold matter, of all these signs none are worth cautery, save for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	If the patient is devoid of foul pills or other similar things, make three lines signed with a pinprick on his back, under the armpits where the pain persists; and burn as many cauteries as he can bear; or as many as seem necessary according to his strength. And let the cautery be performed according to the cautery that is called "poins"; and if you see that he needs it, make two or three cauteries at the middle cautery according to this form.
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes with small inflammations, and signs of beginning are that they are stiff and painful when they happen, and fear; and you find it behind the lower spine on the back and on us it appears like that which comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it cured, if you cauterize at the center according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery touches any part of the spine, it will swell.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, if you cauterize around the spine at the place where the cautery is pricking two or three lines, and keep the points close together.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the wound until it is healed according to what we have said, take care that you do not move the cautery over nerves that are nearby
de la dolor des jointes	When the fire cautery burns some part of the spine, cauterize around the spine at the place where the cautery has pierced. The points should be close together. After the burn is complete, cure the wound until it is healed as we have said, and beware that you do not bring the cautery too close to the nerves.
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the joints are affected by moisture that is spread throughout the limb and when the pain comes from inflammation, that is called "podagre." When the cause is cold and treatment with medicines does not suffice, it can be cured by cautery in part: make the burn around the joint at the painful spot, using olive oil in the following manner:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is need that you prick on the face of the jaw, if you are to cauterize with the whole cautery, say "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is pain that comes up to the groin and other joints, and this happens many times, if you are to cauterize on each knee three cauteries or four of each part, with the whole olive-oil cautery; and if you must do more, do more, but do not keep your hand firm for longer than necessary.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pain descends down to the groin and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pain is as far as the hands, if you prick at the base of the little finger two lines; and if there remains no pain at that point, if you prick above the wrist and below the thumb; and if the pain goes down to the buttocks or to the shoulder blades, if you cauterize some part of it, and make the patient drink something and take medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him drink something and purge phlegm, he will be healed by the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface of the skin
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the shoulder joint comes out of its socket, and the ball descends like a coon, this is new; if you see the cure for this, do not trust it; and if it uses things that leave the belly open, so that the worms descend from the belly; after that, make the patient sit on his back between your hands, and command him to keep his arm stretched out as long as the ball is repaired, and hold it at your two sides, and mark the exit of the shoulder joint from the bony prominence, and as soon as there is any sign that it is like half of a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as he is limp and drowsy.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then bind the belly to its place; and hold his hand above so that it does not return backwards; and give the patient good support to the wound, and put on for him I cushion and I bandage on the wound, and I put another on the hand which holds him; then put the cautery on the sign at all your hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you have reached the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and beware cautiously that the belly does not swell when you are making the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or any other evil thing
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And so it is that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it must be known that the cautery of the small intestines should be subtle according to their measure, and of the great people also great according to their measure; after three days cure the body of the burn until the eschar becomes bony; after that cure other wounds until they are healed; and keep the patient lying for forty days on his back until the wound is well closed; and it must be known that their emissions must be prolonged, so that the feces do not spill when he goes to the chamber.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, let him be accompanied by a well-made servant, and let him rest for forty days; and let him have good rest, that he work little and take care to eat little and drink little, and to avoid excessive laughter; and when he has learned this he is entirely healed
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall speak of the treatment of the tail in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, he will find a well-formed scab, which will last for forty days; and he will have had good rest, so that he will work steadily and take care not to eat too much or drink too much, and not to smoke too much; and when he has followed this teaching, he will be entirely healed. And I will speak of the treatment of boils in this chapter.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When they come out in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, if you do not prick them at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow. After the treatment, according to what we have said; and no one has ever said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the limb and make a line parallel to the belly of the routure, and another perpendicular, and hold your hand firmly with the entire cautery needle.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more fluid.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	But first mark the place with a mark and make a line parallel to the breadth of the wound, and another perpendicular, and hold your hand firmly against the cautery clamp. But the first cauteries are lighter and more fluid.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, or to the hip or to the wound, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the medical treatment is not worth it, then it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called “points,” and the cautery should be done according to the length of the limb and the smallness and weakness and virtue and location of the twisting and the pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sound after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery upon that one, for it is customary that it must swell towards the adjacent limb, so that you may make the cauteries until the patient is sound.
de meselerie	From meselerie
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The diseases are never aided by the cautery, and often the disease which comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cautery? Take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not stay or linger, and you doubt that corruption does not spread throughout the entire sickness, then make five cauteries on the head: one on the new head, and the other towards the front towards the end of the beard; two on the two horns, and one behind on the back; and leave the hand as long as the cauteries come up to the bone, and as long as the scabs come out strong so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is in front of you
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is scattered everywhere; and it appears manifestly, if you must cauterize from these cauteries which we have said or from the chief, and one cauterize in the neck, and two on the spine of the collarbone, and three on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and one other in the groin, and two on the shoulders, and two on the tendons of the arms and legs, and one on each joint of the hands and feet; and beware of the nerves that are on the back of the heel, that you do not burn them; and never make the cautery on the bone of the heel, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the wounds that when more fire cautery is done, the more aid it does, and it benefits them; and the wounds that the patients do not feel any pain from the fire as if they were feeling it, for the flesh is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the fire must be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you saw in dealing with these things
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure of the body from time to time with honey and other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then you must make incisions on the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and either the incisions are made in the flesh or in the bone; and then you must cure it with ointments until it is healed
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never make cautery at the hand and the foot and the back, at the issue of nerves that move the limb, and thus if it is bony it swells; and in any case nothing hinders it unless one is familiar with the limbs and the issues of the moving nerves of the limb.
de albaras	De albaras.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and the physician's remedies are of no avail, then a cautery is to be performed once with a little burn, according to the quantity of the black bile which has come, until the blenchour is bony and its color is altered; then it is to be treated with flour of times, lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and saffron and alum, one part of each; mix them all together and bandage them with a cloth, and keep them until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for fistula by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil starts, and you see it stop, if you cauterize at the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all these people say that we should cauterize also in the middle of the boil; and all these people do not seem to me to be right, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already known several times that it must not be done; and the more correct thing is that it should be cauterized around, at the cautery which is called "circle," as we have said before.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	When there is an inflammation that cannot be measured...
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has an ailment which is called "adubelati," and it delays in healing or because of the excessive heat it causes or because of the sickness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and there is much blood, or for any other reason; and you see that it is hastening to heal: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see the fire cautery burning at its full intensity, if the fire is too hot, the form of the cautery is like this:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries perceive the cold, and be such cauteries as the patient feels heat in parts as they proceed towards corruption to be joyous.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards cure them as long as they are perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another symptom of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing but the softening of a limb, for it softens the bones as fire softens wax.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a limb that can endure fire cautery, then shave the hairs closely and liberally, as much as the limb or the disease allows; after that, cauterize all parts until you have eradicated all corruption, and leave nothing but sound bone.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized limb a bandage soaked in oil until the burnings from the fire are ossified, and all corruption is gone
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of oily inflammations.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days the hair does not grow back, it is good; and if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	This treatment is never cured by water medicine instead of fire cautery; but every time fire cautery is of greater help, as I have already said in the preceding section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Hair that comes out whole like nails.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that when pieces of flesh have departed, a disease called “clos” according to our understanding, and is a great burdensome thing that bleaches the spirit.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery for this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	If thou art scorched by fire, I order thee to cauterize the hair even as is a pine cone; make it of fine iron to the measure that it can penetrate all parts, and there must be a space between the nails; afterwards put all about the head of the nail, and keep thy hand round the nail until it comes to the front of the nail; and leave it for three days until it begins to ooze pus; then make an embolus of bruised wild mallow seeds with wool, and leave the embolus upon the whole night, and bind it firmly and it shall be plucked from its roots.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by boils of foul matter, and often happen in hands and feet, if you must bring a cautery of hot water; it is in part like this: take a flax or iron bowl, or a needle of gutta, and put on the thumb and the little finger, that is to say, burn the nails; and put the bowl on so that it covers everything around, then put a drop of hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the bowl comes to the root of the thumb, and you will find the hot water going deep down to the root; and give the patient a drop of the hot water an hour; then leave it alone, and it will spread throughout all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do another time, until you have scraped away all that is on the limb, and then cure the wounds which are left behind, which cause car.
li cure dou trembler	The cure for tremors.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from another, if it is thought that you should make for them three or four cauteries upon the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades; and one cautery or pinch, and one upon the stomach at the olive cautery; if you leave them to tremble, the sickness will be cured from the cold.
des pustules puans	pusules full of pus.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never do wounds appear by chance; or boils filled with pus, which come from corrupt matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary at the outset when they appear, make cautery on each head of the boils: a subtle cautery of mustard seed, or so that the point is grasped by the fire, or by long aristologue root, or by lenticular cautery.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never do the cauteries begin at the outset when they appear, according to this method, but the blood which is evacuated must be drained, and it is healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.</start_of_turn
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a mournful thing to extend the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens, if you are hasty to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and you strain it out too much without soothing it down, and no blood flows from it; then take the olive cautery and make several small and large burns until they are all red; then touch it, that is to say, make it large or small according to the wound and the limb in which the artery is passing, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your index finger, and hold the cautery as long as it is not fixed.</start_of_turn
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts violently when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take hold of another cautery that is in the fire quickly.</start_of_turn
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the limb is extended; and beware that you do not damage the nerve that is below, and that no other evil arises upon the patient; and that as soon as without drawing blood from an artery, you cannot properly fill himself up again even if the artery is large, except by one of the three methods that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed upon which have power to fill up blood. And let it be bound and strained afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever comes to restore the limb correctly will rest it tightly with bandages or put warm things upon it, or do other similar things, unless it proves of no benefit in that way.</start_of_turn>
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and there is no remedy or medicine present, he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it still as long as it is under the wound and under the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often that it may be cold as long as the limb is frozen and swollen and still. And make incisions before those which require cautery and medicines.</start_of_turn>
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag le second livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said in the first chapter that in all diseases where it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or to apply warming medicine, and to inquire into the lesions and their causes, and the instruments and forms of cautery; and in this chapter we will speak of the most legitimate way to proceed in this work, since we have found it to be lighter in this way than in any other way.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	Moreover, as I have said at the beginning, it is necessary to learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapters of the cautery, and for this reason it is necessary to exercise greater caution.</start_of_turn
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to be rash.</start_of_turn>
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in many ways people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	For in many ways people come to cures. If they come from those who suffer greatly from their ailments and move lightly because of the discomfort of their disease, and from the greatness of their suffering; one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And concerning these things, some make sense and say: "Wait, I am going away"; and the disease is despicable
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	I must only tell you that those who come to your presence must be allowed to do so; but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not trust me foolishly more than prudently about what you are certain of, and what you have taken and lost; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation is either recovered or transformed; and this will help you to obtain good renown, glory, and long memory
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Sirs, your do well to understand and judge, and if you are filled with the spirit of the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.</start_of_turn>
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selon ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have ordered thee this chapter by chapters, according to what is before or after the cautery, that I have ordered thee from the head down to the toes, because thereby thou shalt find it more conveniently than what thou hast to do.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Saiches that this disease comes out many times at childbirth, and when the babe’s bail is strained too strong the head of the babe; and never comes from a known cause except that one does not know it.</start_of_turn>
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease vanish except in the spring, and with all that I have heard, it seems to me that it is worth leaving the work in parts for cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen many times in my childhood when the head of the shoulder was dislocated due to moisture, and the head grew so large that it could not support itself; and I believed so much moisture that it became blood, and this moisture if it is gathered between the bones above the scapula, between the shoulder blade and the arm; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the shoulder blade and the arm, and the incision is small, that you must make a wide incision; and be as long as .ij. we have seen, until the moisture has gone; and when this is done, the shape of the scapula will be like that of a spindle.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture is excessive and swells the bone, and if you see the corners of the bone protrude in the lower part, and if it causes pain that increases when you press your hand inwards, and this does not subside: if you suspect that the bone is fractured, make two incisions as described in this manner.
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out all the moisture with force.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After that, drain out the blood clots and humours, and give wine and oil, and leave in place for five days; then remove the dressing, and cure the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the head of the limb elevated, and give the patient dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another method of incision is to look or open the apex of the abscess, and gather the fluid; for it is never in front; never behind; never to the right; and never to the left.</start_of_turn>
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.
de reume	When the shoulder joint is dislocated and the opening is wide, and the injection of liquid, and you do according to what you are able; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known ailment that is called "cataract," and there are pus or white spots, and the disease is ancient, and the medical cure does not help, then the only remaining cure is to cauterize with that which covers the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary to do this quickly, for you cannot see the patient’s head covered; after that, rub the limb with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then pull out the patient’s neck with all the strength; then look to see if the vein is open, and if the veins are below the ears, then restore them; then mark the veins, then ligate the one and the other with a needle of two parts, until the size of the vein reaches the bone, and this is done by the large hole of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see, hold the sponge under the artery and press above, cutting as much as two thumbs together to pierce through.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if the blood spurts continuously upwards, keep pressure on it without interruption.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open on examination, if you can, measure the amount of space of three fingers; then mark and stop just above the bone; and what is necessary put forth if there is six fingers, or a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the refill of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the bone where the sutures have come loose, if the skin covering the stitches has not healed, then strain the wound and tie it up, and keep it bound until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open on sensing it, if you think it is two fingerbreadths wide, mark its end and advance until bone is reached; what is to be done with blood that spurts out if it is more than two fingerbreadths, or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the edges of the incisions do not reunite, then strain the wound and ligate it, and cure it with dressing until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dropsy comes, and acute fever, because of tears and the heat in temples and old saliva forsened and similar things, it is treated by means of medical cures and everything that does not help, if we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And thus the manner of extracting them is that the patient should make the hair of his temples grow long; and he should understand the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating; and is much more easily restored than in some men who are too cold. And if it is restored, he should strain his neck the patient of some cloth, then wipe the area with no rough cloth, and raise the area with warm water until the artery opens openly; then take the sponge which is like this:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then pull the skin gently until you reach the artery, then draw it upwards with hooks, and remove the cloths that are under the armpit; and if the artery is tense, if the nail has a point at the elbow, then clamp that part according to the quantity of two fingers.</start_of_turn>
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not well joined, if it does not leap without doubt in all things.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Then he should drain blood from the armpits, up to two inches; and if the artery is large, it is expedient to ligate it with two strong silk threads, so that no blood will be seen in front of the wound, and the blood will drain away; then cauterize the surplus that is between the two ligatures in that place, and then, if you see, burn the hair with a fine cautery until the hair is cut; and this is the best remedy, if the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.</start_of_turn>
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is helpful to finish off moisture: for this is more helpful with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is useful to extract the arteries that are full of fat and put on well-made stitches; and when you take them out, if you are cured of dry medicines that cause char and stitches, as long as you are sane; and if without support of the artery as you must do if you do this too quickly, or if you touch the vessel with the vitriol, it will stain your hand; and if you do not have this, you must take out the vessel until it is frozen, and rise the cold water until it stops, and strain as much as it is possible; and what is more limp and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein of this cautery at a distance of .ij. inches, but the incision must be well spaced to prevent lasting too long its heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery must have between the joints a space of one inch; and when you have marked the area with a needle, you must let the fire burn until it reaches the bone, and then close the vein with one inch of leathers; and let the hair be plucked out between the needles, for it is not soldered by this cautery in any way; and this is the form of the fire cautery.

Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	For if it is not well joined, if it does not leap without doubt in all things. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that causes pain in the ears is one of three things: grains, or boils, or stone or similar objects like iron; or seeds, like lice, beans, peas; or fluid things like vinegar and urine and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it happens in the ear lobe or any other way that does not fit with the ear, do not put it in the ear, but put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if no black speck of oil of violet or oil of chamomile appears, then order the extraction; and let him vomit forcefully, and stop his nose when he vomits, and put in his ear pieces of cloth or wool; and hold the ear down.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times comes forth with this treatment; and if it does not come forth, order the extraction of fine needles, for this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out by these needles, it is well done; if not, seek extraction with fine needles of double curvature; and if it does not come out by this, make an incision of an inch and a half and cut off the chief of the incision or pierce the ear very deeply, and squeeze out what is around the incision mole if it comes out with the incision; then the pain will disappear, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out partly, take hold of the bone with your thumb and index finger and put under no instrument that has a point for this purpose, and put a patch of cotton around; then press the thumb on the bone or whatever it is, and the pain will go away.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If these things do not suffice, if you are in a hurry to make an incision at the ear-lobe along with the abscess chalaz, and spasm, do this: first make the patient comfortable and loosen the hair of the head; then sit the patient between your hands and turn the ear downwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fatty or glandular tissue; and let the incision be as wide as a crescent, as long as you live to the bone, and the bone according to your will; and evacuate the pus immediately from your mouth.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If grains are seen which are swollen and inflamed, administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, administer sponge-rubber tightly according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and order the incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in their ears; and the same thing happens as adults with wounds or tumors that protrude into the ear, for these protrusions never come out of the ear unless they are seen; and never is there such a thing as perfectly formed ears.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Whenever they protrude into the ear without being seen, it is a sign of serious illness in many cases; and in this case it is clear that you put the diseased ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the swelling, if the swelling has filled the whole cavity as far as it can, then it is formed like this:

de la gresle	From the bark of the tree.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come out of paper things that seem to bristle in their form and in their hardness, and because of this is this disease called "granule", and is an assembly of great moisture in the marrow of bones; the work is such: take warning when the granuloma moves from one side to the other, and that is a light thing to know; do then the large dose, then score the soft part lightly, then take as many pins as you please, and hold.</start_of_turn>
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not see the wound covered with hair, if you do not grieve the patient; and if the wound is large, if the collection has a curvature, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, for the swelling will restore itself soon and heal faster.</start_of_turn
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulinea descends downwards from the ear towards the upper part, if you reverse the marrow, extend the granulinea with tweezers, grasp and press from one side and the other; and if the marrow is loosened by the incision, this will cause no harm; and when the granulinea is grasped, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the limb of that which causes harm until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the blood.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is enclosed in paper tissues, and this occurs more in those who have no nails, and grieve much for their eyes, and they come to tears at dawn, and cannot bear to see the sunlight because the tears hurry to their eyes; and because of this they lie with their faces down, and sleep on, and their paper tissues are soaked with moisture that swells and appears covered in exinach which bursts in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb to your chest and feel the exinach between the bones.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	When the patient puts his hand in his bosom; then take one cloth of linen, and make a circle with your thumb according to the quantity of wax in the chest; then put it on; then press with your thumbs from one side and the other, so that the wax is gathered into a circle; then make an incision about the width of a vein, without making it any larger than the wound made in the vein; and when you have finished, the wax comes out of the incision, according to the form of a white lump of fat.</start_of_turn>
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the lump entirely with a sharp knife between your thumbs, and turn your hand to the right and left as much as possible; and keep that you do not touch the edges, until you have reached the bottom; that you do not stain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the dislocation does not reappear at the start of the wound, if you expand the wound slightly until it opens; then draw out the foreign body as we have said, and moisten with wool and water, and place back in the limb, and strain the bandage.

des poilz des papieres	hair of papers</start_of_turn>
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like substances grow hair-like, adjust them from their natural state and they are enveloped; if they prick the eyes, they cause tears and produce various diseases like common weeping and softening of paper and mucus, up to the point of destroying the eyes; and the cure for this is in three ways: either by entire fire cautery, or by water-based medicine as it is before or alongside fire cautery, or by incision and stitching or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s chief in your left hand, then draw out the paper from your right hand; if it is softened, it is well done; if not, if there is an awl with every thread of hair below; either cut the margin of the paper or the hair grows out below those hairs, and draw out one thread at the root of every hair; then press on the lower part of the paper, pressing out the hairs that have been adjusted, over the entire area up to the great tear until the small one; then draw out one thread and put a small patch of cotton and bandage on the paper, then mark on the paper a figure like a spurge, like the spurge of myrtle, and it is enough that the figure be according to the quantity you see raising the paper that is designed for you.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If it comes to the vein of the armpit, if the cure for embolism is applied while it is still sane, and if there is much blood in the middle, then take hold of the two lines that you have marked and stretch out all the flesh from the two armpits to the groin; then make a wound near the root of the hair, and bring the ointment to one of the two angles downwards, then pull out the hair; then gather the two layers together with a suture of fine thread, and wipe away the surplus of thread from the two edges, as you see me do; and if this does not suffice, do not hesitate to leave the suture and the thread for three days or four; then cure the wound with dry and constrictive things, for the blood returns to its place at the bottom of the wound and the gathering together of it, but the suture is useless (as they say the old ones), and this is a dangerous operation. And if there is another method: and it is that you mark the blood with a figure which is as big as the berry of a mistletoe flower, as we have been told, with three lines that are drawn according to this form.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then close what is above with small forces evenly according to the form that is here
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the teeth firmly, and the matter is not equal, take a needle or two, and pass one thread through the figure; and pass another thread loosely from the great loop, and the second thread loosely from the small loop, and join the two threads together equally; then keep your hand equally, and keep all the skin that you have marked, as we have told you, and join the two layers of the wound together with stitches, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerate and some soothing and absorbent dressings. And never again will there be any hair left on the wound: if you follow what we have said concerning the incision; but the stitches in one and the other are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for varicose veins is as follows: convert the armpit hair and fat according to what has been said, then make three veins by art, and two fine threads as long as the hair and as wide as a sparrow's foot; and take three hairs from three parts or hold the threads. Then assemble the one and the other securely above what rests on the oil of the hair, and strain the two veins from the two parts forward; and leave it like that for a few days. The leather which has been strained will rot and decay and will become loose, until it disappears by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has strength, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is closed and if the wound has risen, and the hair will no longer grow; and this is the form of two nails that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is thus: take a subtle hook, and there is in it a thread of silken thread. Then join the hooks together and do not twist one with the other; and let the length of the threads be equal. Then order in the chase another thread of silken thread briefly, and do not twist them together. Then put the patient's thumb in its place. And let there be no shadow if the work is completed, for it is a subtle and small work. Then draw out the hook at the whole chase until it pierces in the root of the hairs with the natural position. Then withdraw the hair until there remain one or two or three or more. Then withdraw your hand until the vein is fully exposed at the whole chase with the natural position.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from its pierce and you see it by the light of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two days or three, until the hair has healed in its place and the wound has closed.

de la char qui vient en l’oil	De la char qui vient en l’oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called by the swelling that really is known as "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large. dou soudement de la papiere	If the ailment comes from a fracture or sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a complete incision over the hair and cover with paper; then withdraw between the two books of a tent, as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know well everything that pertains to making the figure return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is proper in more diverse situations.

de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil

des voines des eulz	Des voines des eulz
