puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	The veins of the eyes are two in number and are graduated by degree in one inch in this form:
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If thou canst not collect all this in that hour, make an embalmment upon oil of soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave them thus until the pain is appeased and is assured from aftercare; then begin again in this manner as before until they are healed; and that is the form of safety.
de la fistule de l’oil	If thou canst not collect all this in that hour, make an embalmment upon oil of soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave them thus until the pain is appeased and is assured from aftercare; then begin again in this manner as before until they are healed; and that is the form of safety.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	If thou canst not collect all this in that hour, make an embalmment upon oil of soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave them thus until the pain is appeased and is assured from aftercare; then begin again in this manner as before until they are healed; and that is the form of safety.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is fractured, and you see the corruption and blackness, if the limb has all the characteristics of this form, it is called "aspire chief," and is made of ivory, that is, a chief rent, or pointed as with a file when it is in this form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And lay on the limb the fractured bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand until you sense that the corruption is gone; do this only once, then restore the limb to the exiccative medicine.</start_of_turn>
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the limb is stiff and does not move, and the hair has not yet begun to grow, and the root of the bow is stiff, and remains so for XL days, and does not recover or improve, even after dressing and repositioning, and the patient is well; if this is not the case, if there is no other remedy except to restore the fistula to its natural position, uncover the bone a second time by fire, and by sharp medicines. And when you have uncovered it take hold of the limb at its three angles, and the limb must be reduced to its normal position as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put your thumb on the bone below the armpit, and withdraw your hand from the oil, and draw back your arm until it breaks the bone and the patient feels it through that which comes out from under his arm if he holds his hand on his elbow; and when the bone breaks and becomes firm, if there is anything at the elbow; if it is lighter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Then place your thumb on the bone below the armpit, and wipe your hand with oil. Immediately, straighten your arm until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through his hand which is resting on his elbow. Then restore the dry medicine to its place, as I have taught you, and when the wound is healed and firm, if there is still any matter in the elbow; if it is a lighter matter for the patient.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound is open from all sides, and there is no danger of displacement of the bowels, no reduction, if you must bind the patient; then stretch the limb, and put on compresses or a dressing in the direction of the wound, then apply oil.i. with acaice and aloe and incense and ochre, then strain the oil and put it on pads and bandages; and keep the bandages if you take bandages thick enough, and double chescun in .iiij., and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity of oil there is in the wound; then strain by pressing down on a stiff bandage. Repeat the compresses in the direction of the wound. Then support the compresses and leave the oil strained for a night, and if the limb is relaxed, if you remove it by mouth; then support the limb again after the night and morning, and if you see the oil returning, that is good; if not, repeat the dressing and bandages and the limb and the compresses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Dou derrompement de toile uvee
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the dislocation comes in the shoulder and is forced open, and there comes forth paper like barley grains; it is expected to see; then if you see it covered, the work is like biting a needle at the root of the lower part until under that, and then insert another needle or there is a double thread of the lower part; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle as it lies; then join the double thread and bind a part of the upper arm, and strain it well, then draw out the needle and put on oil cloth soaked in eggs; and leave it as long as the thread remains with the shoulder, and cure the oil of comfortable things until the wound is healed; and never restrain the wound by the shoulder strap part of a circle of silk, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has great appearance, if you prick at the soft tissue which comes from behind the oil, and correct the moistness of the albumin and pull down the wound, and enter inside; then draw it out as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	The ailment called "alcunnati" is not fierce except for the swelling which is composed in oil, resembling descending ice, and it is not actually ice; and the manner in which it appears is that if you make the patient sit on the apparent and straight seat, and grasp the chief between your hands two parts, and move it as long as you see the swelling coming down towards your eyes; then either bind it, and do not let it descend, or break the light, and see the patient the things as he alone would see; and if it does not descend even after that, like ice, it appears as if we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the corner of the conjunctiva with the edge of the sponge against the conjunctiva and the crown, as long as the eye is closed; and when the eye opens, distillate into hot water mixed with honey, or into vinegar or fenugreek boiled with honey, then be cured of another remedy until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the bowl of oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similar things in the case of fever, and what it is necessary to know; if in this case one should follow the advice of the physician.</start_of_turn>
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, expose the eye to the sunlight, and apply the pure oil; then put the bandage on the thumb of your left hand if the eye is left, or on the thumb of your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called the almond, or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the point of the instrument below the crown by the thickness of a finger in the amount of oil in the lower part of the tear, then push the instrument called the almond well, and restore your hand until it pierces in the amount of oil, and feel that the almond has come to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almond be equal to the measure of the space from the prune to the end of the black; and that is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that bandage by the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument until it is flat or the water is there, and then press the oil out a way afterwards.</start_of_turn>
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it seems to him that the patient is awake now, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a little rest, if he seems awake again, if he sees the patient before him and the instrument in his oil, grasp the limb firmly with the instrument. When it is firmly fixed and does not move, if it is necessary, stretch the limb slightly by circling your hand around it from below and above; then reintroduce the water and remove the oil from the wound.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by force the oil-soaked bandage or cloth in oil rose and in abundance of eggs, and bind with the clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Indeed, and those who are of our kind, put on coming broth with abundance of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda will not enter the oil because there are parts of flesh that have too thick hair, it is expedient that you take the instrument which is called the «alberit», which is like this:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva slightly, and do not make me move too much, but make him wink, then I will stretch, as we have said; and when the work is finished appears the patient to me sleeping on his back in a dark room; and let him have no movement, and give him soft foods, and do not move his head to the right or left, and bind him according to his disposition until the seventh day; then take him out of this house into the open air, and uncover his face, and make him see nothing, and then put him back in his bed until the seventh day; and do not let me do anything else except in the hour of treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you feed him, because he has suffered enough.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Leave the oil undone before the seventh hour, and apply it to that which soothes the abscess; and when it is settled, remove the bandage and put a little oil on the wound to cover any hole, and keep it closed in that dark place.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go out of the house slowly and gradually, and if necessary; let the maidservant stay away from this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from Iraq who said that in his land they used to make an almagda of oil every day, when the pain occurred, but we have never seen or read of it in our land or in the books of the ancients; and it is a new thing for us

Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like a goosefoot.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint on the neck.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never are born or come out various ointments, because there are some which seem like scorpions at the root of the teeth; and if there are such or if there is hair entangled with dark fur and if there is hair of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those cases where these hairs are blunt and do not entangle, you must make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; and cover his nose and spit out the vomit onto those hairs, and drive out the urine; for it will support the delicate spleen from the sharp pain of the spur.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to hold it, if the opening has reached its utmost extent, if nothing is left to hold; and if without being warned, or by incision, if any support fails, if it is a malignant abscess, hasten and cauterize as much as possible until the surrounding tissue is unstained and all the vessels are closed. Then withdraw or do not withdraw easily or with pain or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he does not work, and moisture comes up to his palate, saliva which is sane; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, saliva which is in the root of the teeth above, because the instruments do not come out whole: then it must be that you drink a large thread of linen, and hold it with your hands, and leave between each knot no space at all; and put the patient’s head over the thread at the front, and treat it by smelling until it comes out through the mouth; and often they do this to the children, and it is a light matter for one who has seen it done; then take the fist which comes through the mouth with one hand, and the other fist which comes through the nose with the other hand, and grasp one after the other while holding as we are or with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it may be of silver or of brass, resembling a broad lamp, like a cauldron; and you shall carry it thus; and if you see, make a closed loop, and the instrument will be flat for purging the head; and hold one hand at the head and the other at the mouth to hold when we burn the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the head of the neck a disease which is called "telul," and it grows and becomes great at once, so that it is visible; and for this reason it is necessary that you should begin to seize it at the outset, and break the bone thoroughly, then remove the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay in seizing it when it is great, if you take hold of it with force, of foul colour, of bad omen: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a fleshy swelling, for when you seize it once, there comes great harm to the patient; and if the swelling is of soft touch, not of foul colour, you can see that you can seize it all, if you evacuate the patient and seize it without fear, and cure the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do not leave the wound open any longer than necessary; then draw out the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balsam, and reinsert it as before; do this for three days or more, until the abscess has dissolved all that is remaining; and then put in or withdraw a sponge for a few days until it is healed, and if there is any need for sedative medicines, use them. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, from which oils and medicines or nois are distilled.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it has happened to anyone, if the wound is fresh throughout its entirety; then join the two levers to a bolster, and hold them until they are healed; and if the levers are already detached from one side and the other, if you can, support all the parts around their root until they bleed, then reassemble the two levers to a bolster, and strain, and sprinkle upon them powdered dragon's blood, and incense smoke; and place upon the powders a piece of plaster of strong or another plaster that binds, and leave it until it bleeds by itself, then cure it when it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the staple is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we said in the costure of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the edges of the wound.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home in the hands, there are from the thumbs to the little finger nails of varying sizes, some like grains of wheat, minor and greater; therefore when you turn the fingers, make incisions on each nail, and grasp with tweezers and hold in the palm of the hand; then employ the blood from the incision of a broken vein, until it is no longer bleeding; and then withdraw the tweezers easily, and cure the hand of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the ridge of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times appears on the gums a fleshy bulge which the ancients called "albulus"; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the swelling or bleeding to subside; then remove the broken vein or other powdery astringents and drying agents; and if that fleshy bulge recurs after the incision, and happens many times, if you grasp it a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Once are gathered at the head of the teeth, between the gums, escorces which are soft and rough; and never are the teeth black and yellow and gray, until the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are biting; if it is that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his shoulder bones be in their place, and open the gums or the escorces open, until there is nothing left; and thus make black and green, and yellow and other spots, until they are whole; and if one has what is at the first reason, it is good; if not, if it begins again to rise the second and third time, until you have done everything; and teeth that have met with various forms of instruments to redden, as it is shown by the work, for those who have scraped whose teeth have other forms than those which are between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you apparent.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you stay quiet for a long time, because it must not make me do it; for it is a high-quality substance so we have no excuse for making excuses
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is constrained due to pain, if you can, be certain that he will endure it.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient complains of pain, and cares either that it is acute or chronic, and makes him groan; and all this while he does not feel the pain for this, as long as the disease persists, for we have already wanted to do these things to these scoundrels; and when you are certain that he will endure it, if you can, support his teeth firmly to prevent any movement from front to back; then grasp his two thumbs or index fingers at the first joint and hold them firmly until they are well established, then firmly secure the nails; and let the patient's hand rest between your thighs, and hold it firmly so that it does not move
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, draw the tooth directly downwards towards the briser; and if it does not yield, take none of these instruments and press it inwards lightly, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and inflamed, if it is necessary, cover it with cloths, or take away the cause; and if the pressure is made too hard, it will break through the pressure; and it is necessary to keep the tooth moist around the gum with saliva.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first.</start_of_turn>
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware that you do not act stupidly like the ignorant layman, who without haste and without courage break the limb many times without result, and do not bring about what we have said; but they bring about many times by the cause of that great illness from the roots that remain, or from the limb itself that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the blood of wine or vinegar and oil; and if there is bleeding, as often happens, apply the powder of vitriol burnt; and if that does not suffice, cauterize.</start_of_turn
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, indeed mute the hands at first, whether with long points and thick sleeves, that they do not double when you draw the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick limbs so that they do not bend when drawing, and be of iron well made, and be toothy so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains fixed at the back, if you must put out the moist cotton swab, take out either the thumb or the index finger.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the limb is stiff, because there are teeth that are split and appear like bristles; and that they are made in the same way as with a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not suffice to endure these tensions, if you must uncover the bark throughout the root, and put the instrument which is called «althali», which is to say a palatine, since this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and bulky if it does not break me, and if the root leaps by this, it is good; if not, if you help with all the instruments, since these shapes will come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has .ij. rings, since this is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the rank of teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Or other instruments which are before in the rank of teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Or be great and well-holding to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this, and if there is inflammation in the bone, if it is small, if the wound has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears does not follow the natural curve, and its shape is deformed, even in women of childbearing age, if it is dense enough to impede its eruption, it will not rise properly, and it cannot be remedied: therefore it must be extracted. And if it is associated with the tooth, if you take hold of this instrument which has the shape of a small beak, resembling a file, and grasp it with iron tongs, so be it.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the pain persists in the jaws and the hands for as long as the tooth lasts, and because of that you must not move the others, and if it appears, it can be limed, if you file a part of the lime like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is just like filing nails; and while you are filing the tooth slightly in the jaws and hands, if it does not move at all, when you finish the piece at the end there is no raiser, and if the cavity is too deep and it blisters the tongue, if you must file the rough spot so that it is even, so that it does not blister the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth comes loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, by percussion or biting, and the patient cannot press against what is painful, and you must cure them with restrictive medicines, this is of no use; if you can restrain them with a gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and corrupts, but the bone does not move; and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth leaning, if you take hold of the wire and double it between the two front teeth, then put the teeth between the middle teeth, if there is one or more of them, until you see them straight up to the other tooth; then finish the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and cautiously, until it does not move; and let the bandage be bound to the root of the tooth if it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the arm with a pair of forceps, assemble and insert it between the teeth of the jaw, and hold it until it stops bleeding; and then leave it alone as much as it can remain in place, and if it slips or the thread breaks, strain it with another thread; if it persists and serves its purpose, that is the form of a tooth and the figure of the arrangement of the two front teeth, and the two lower teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you reset it anew, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and do not let anything interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make the shape of a tooth of a whale bone; put it back in its place or where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and keep it in place for a long time with firm pressure.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Under no circumstances does this happen because of infection of the tongue or the natural condition, that we are born without; or by accident of a deep wound; and the work is such that you must cause the patient to open their mouth wide, and touch their tongue, and hold the tongue; then grasp the large nerve that is beside the tongue, until the tongue is displaced from its dwelling place, and if there is delay or no improvement, and that is the sign of an infected wound, if it comes to the opening of the wound and grasp the large thread; and keep that the opening is not too deep, because of the artery that is beside; and when you have done this, if you lift the pale and easy blood, or cold blood, then put the tongue in a spasm of linen; and keep the patient quiet, so that the bleeding stops.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes from the wound, take out the glass vessel that is bleeding; and if it does not stop, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see red or black or hard pus coming from it, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a fistula; and if it is declining with moisture, if it is spitting blood, if you touch the wound, and deliver from a part and from the other; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on a glass splinter until it is clean, and then come back to your work until you have finished everything; then lift the limb easily and gently, and cure with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes comes from the throat black tongues which are called "godath", and they are properly two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if they are abscesses of small size and colour of soot, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, even though there is bleeding; but leave it until it has stopped bleeding, and then you can remove it, or it will break on its own; and if it is white in colour and the root is thin, if you have applied the instrument to cover, but first look to see if the abscess has settled and is calm
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fais seoir le patient devant le soleil, ses bras soient en position naturelle, il bouche la bouche et prend les serjans entre ses mains, et presse la langue doucement contre tous les instruments, car ainsi est la forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi comme une aiguille.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	... press his tongue down with all your might: this is the way. And let it be of silver or of gold like a needle. Can you press the tongue down with all of this instrument? And you see the clot: take the sponge and press it into the almond, and pull it out more forcefully than you can. And do not put anything on the cloth with it. Then remove the instrument from the clot, as this is the way it is done. The chief is bent in many places, and one part is over the other, and they are very acute, and is made of iron or gold.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with your thumbs, know that this is its form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you can grasp it with your thumbs, know that this is its form: grasp the thumb and index finger together, and when you have grasped one of the thumbs, grasp the other in the same way, and then make an incision and gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when the blood has drained out, if there are still blood clots, either break them up with nutmeg seeds or burn them with cloves of garlic, or fumigate with marjoram, and the like; until the wound is healed; and never again shall there be any further bleeding from the incision except for the two thumbs, if you grasp them just as before.</start_of_turn>
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, arms in their natural position, cover the mouth and grasp the thumbs between the hands, pressing the tongue gently against all the instruments, for this is the form; and be of silver or gold as fine as a needle.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had forced out two pints through the two holes that were not closed.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I had done so much, and remained in one place, having incised it; then the fire went up, and took a great portion of my bow; then I repeated the operation in another place where I did not feel it, and I closed the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I repeated the incision in these abscesses, and closed a part of them, and only a little blood escaped; and the woman who was beside me loosened the cord of the throat, and now I began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to tear at this abscess for a long time; and the abscesses would rejoin together again, filling up my stomach as much as I could; and at that moment I engaged and cauterized it inside the throat: at that moment it seemed to turn back; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to me after that.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb hangs down, and it is fleeing and is long, it is called "perpendiculaire"; and if it is thick and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the previous section, and the wound does not benefit, and you see that the stitches are relaxed, and it is subtle, if it is thick and gathered and is not long; and if it is bloodstained or dark yellow or black, if you must avoid the incision of the vein.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, as I have said, according to the manner that I have mentioned, that you make the patient sit in the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which I mentioned earlier; then put on the ointment on the limb, and draw out the wound, and close with two sutures that I mentioned in the incision of the two thumbs.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must know that you must not cover more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, if it grieves the voice and the jaw; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two amandres, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, you must know that you must use something to restrain the bleeding in the sense of the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery if it is acute is harsh.

Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as with an incision, comes from an artery and a vein, comes from an incision as soon as it is formed, or by too great a work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And thus it often happens with attendants and those who are two or more in number that there are joints that are affected, and this is the cause of postmortemes, and its color resembles the color of honey, and is in many cases accompanied by pain; and when it is strained, if it causes pain to the patient, it is not in proportion to the honey color, but rather like lead; and it becomes dull from all sides, neither going forward nor backward, neither upwards nor downwards, and the one who is in the joints cannot be held fast by iron: by chance there will be contraction; and if the one who is at the head or the front touches or grasps the leather with his thumb.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the postmortem is small, if the thumb has a nail, hold it in its root; and if it is large, if it hangs in the flesh, and swells, then the bone must be broken and the wound sutured at the edge, and the cure must be continued until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	with great bleeding.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never has it been in the belly and nowhere else that I have seen such a thing that resembles a fungus; its root is subtle and its head is large. And in it are many small and large drops. I know of a home where two out of three bellies were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thick root, and were full of water.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found in one XVIII ounces and in the other VI and a third. And the work in the incision is if the patient is moist, and the color of the areole is pale and moist and has a thick root; if the tumor is large and you are present, apply the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the root comes often too great a discharge of blood, and if it does not go away, if you hurry, then indeed you must cauterize; and if you see the patient groaning and fainting from the incision of the flesh, take a good thread of silk and ligate the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then bind, and do not cease to drain the thread until it has stopped the bleeding; and when the root is black, if there is fear of contamination throughout, take hold of the same again for the belly, but take hold of half only, then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep only the thread that is of firm color and little sense and milk-yellow.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a hairy swelling, and I will come to the treatment of the swelling later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is fierce.</start_of_turn
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the swelling appears by cautery of wound or fracture of bone, and is on the belly and there are some pus, as it often happens in other parts, or blood which clots from veins or arteries as it happens in front, or swelling; and if it is through the bone and by the issue of the bowel, if it is of the color of the spleen, it is a light matter concerning pain, and opens from diverse issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	If it is by the discharge of the intestine, then it is more diverse; and when it is pressed from its two sides, if it returns and comes back again, and by chance if it is tight, and causes swelling at the entrance of the bath and much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is by moisture, it is a light matter, and opens easily when you press on it with your hand; do not constrain me. If it is by blood, if it opens with these signs, the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to quantity. If it is by wind, if it is rough at the touch, and the work is that you see that it is by the blood of an artery or a vein, or the wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you suspect that it is by moisture, it is a light matter, and opens easily when you press on it with your hand; do not constrain me.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said or as the chapter has said, concerning abscesses, of the artery and of the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If the intestine or the bowel appears, command the patient to hold his breath, and stretch it out straight, then mark around the circumference; then grasp it between your hands, then pull out the half of the abscess that extends below the great joint; then bind it firmly with a strong thread or strong silk cord tightly, and secure it; then bring half of the abscess that extends above the thread to your index finger and the intestine; if you find it grasped by the thread, if you loosen it, draw the intestine away from the belly; if you find the bowel, if you grasp it at the navel, and cut off the excess; if the artery opposes this, or the vein, if it goes limp, then go back to your work and take two needles, and take two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have done in the form of a cross that you make pierce; then strain the abscess for three days on the needles, and if you see, break the needles, and leave the limb as long as it swells, and cut off the dead flesh by itself; or you can cut it when it is subtle and swollen, and cure the limb of what it comes to, and close the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the limb of what it comes to, and bandage the limb.
dou chancre	soothe the abscess.</start_of_turn>
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the preceding chapters the signs of an abscess, and how it should be treated by medicine and how it should be cauterized; and we say that an abscess is in the marrow, and that great caution should be used in its cure, and that the old people say that when an abscess is in the bone or can be scraped out as when an abscess is in marrow, and in the hip, and similar things, and that it must be removed as soon as it begins; and when it is large and old, if it cannot be cured but must be approached, for I know of no cure for it; none have ever cured it before me.</start_of_turn>
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And in the work, when it is in place or we can remove it, as we have said, let the patient purge no more than once the black bile; then make him whole if he shows any fullness; then give him wine to make the work; then discharge his vomitings or sores, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb from your hand or from anything else, and if it comes loose from the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize too much without it being stained; then treat him of another remedy until he is healed.
de ydropisie	And in the work, when it is in place or we can remove it, as we have said, let the patient purge no more than once the black bile; then make him whole if he shows any fullness; then give him wine to make the work; then discharge his vomitings or sores, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and expect well the limb from your hand or from anything else, and if it comes loose from the incision of the artery or vein, if you cauterize too much without it being stained; then treat him of another remedy until he is healed.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Nos avons dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et celle qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces deux semblances: c’est à savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines cette semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il y a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let two parts suffice.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let two parts suffice. When you insert the hook into the flesh, do not let it slip so that it comes out into the intestines; look whether the dropsy has descended towards the intestines: if so, if you make an incision three fingers broad on the left side of the belly button, and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, make your incision on the left side; and if it is due to bile, make your incision on the right side. Do not let the patient rest on the incision except for the small amount of blood that will flow out. Then pierce the skin with the instrument and grasp the hook, as you would grasp a nail or a thorn; then pierce the membrane until the hook comes out whole; that is the cause of the pain, then withdraw the instrument and leave the wound open.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver needle, and is of barley or barley chaff lighter, and has at the lower part a little hole; and where it costs one part, three holes; and two from another part, and one from another; and the head of the shoulder is cut off like a quill, and this is the form of the incision which the writer makes to cut off the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the marrow, so that when the instruments approach the apex, if they descend too much on the instruments; empty out half or a third part, for if you empty out more than that at this time, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the wound, or he bleeds, or approaches death; but empty out according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue to the patient signify, and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the blood, which is retained now by the spur that I have mentioned, that you pierce according to this manner; then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering from this, and draw out a small quantity of blood; do this for neither way, and be careful not to use it until it stops bleeding.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient and see him spitting out water, if the surgeon performs the cure for the sepulture or sand cautery, and by spitting out saliva or bath and sun, and if you keep drinking; and let the surgeon give desiccative medicines until he is sane, and cauterize on the stomach and the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	From the swelling of the limb.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Never are children born without a mark in the belly, or the mark is small, or it is not firmly in its place
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If he coves too much, so that he has not perceived for a long time at all the things that he has swallowed according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or perforate the belly of the plonc, and bind and hold it for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if you leave it closed, he will urinate and then you can put it back; and by chance it will not be able to close, because the urine that comes out will not leave it closed
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, if it is medicine with lead weights, as we have said, if it swells up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the opening does not reach the middle of the vessel, the hair is black, for no hair is born which has the root at the base of the beard, because it cannot urinate before it raises its beard up; and it cannot enter without that the matter can come down to the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus the work must be if the patient lies prone upon his back, for the head of the shoulder and the scapula are equal in size to a thumb; if the former breaks through the middle, if as it should be; and you must hold back the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if you can staunch the bleeding of that which bleeds blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	And thus the work must be if the patient lies prone upon his back, for the head of the shoulder and the scapula are equal in size to a thumb; if the former breaks through the middle, if as it should be; and you must hold back the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if you can staunch the bleeding of that which bleeds blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times come these white spots in the armpit, and are an appearance of bad blood; and there are both malignant and benign ones; if it is thought that you should take them out, that is to say, ligate them secretly, and cut off their heads and roots, then put on moist cotton in Egyptian fashion; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is malignant, of dark color and pus-filled, it is recommended that you bring cautery there.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.
