When you have grasped it, and if the abscess is between the shoulder and the elbow, and has part inside the bone and part outside, it is recommended that you reduce the abscess which is inside first; and when it is loosened, if the wound is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure the whole thing together, if it is not firmly secured, the head of the shoulder will soon be perceived [as loose]; and will cause blackness and corruption in the bone and marrow; if you cover all that is black and corrupt, then lie upon the dressing of honey and flour which is made from the rind of pomegranates and sometimes, then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes away, if you mix the lunar cautery with this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps in two positions together: that is, at the discharge of blood, and at corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and retracted, if you bathe or draw out the hair a fingerbreadth at a time, and urinate the patient among them; and when the hair has gone away from the root of the hair which have not been circumcised, or if there is wound or incision, if you must indeed burn them, until the ligament is untied, and deliver the head of the shoulder from all parts; and if it is necessary to divide this, if you must indeed burn it at the navel, without leaving a trace of hair or skin. Then sprinkle well between these two, and put a fine bandage of moist linen on it, cold water.
de la circoncision	De la circoncision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a matter of continuing treatment as with other wounds; however, when it is our work, we must do it with all our will, and promptly, if necessary, for our patients' well-being is more important than our reputation.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach us about circumcision, for they did not use it in their laws, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I would say that the greatest part of masters and healers who performed circumcision were fools. Indeed, there were forces and hurdles, and for all their learning, if the patient ran away because of the discomfort of the two towels, or if by chance the surgeon happened to cut too deep and left the wound open.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, and the pain is doubled, and at the loosening which is done too carelessly, the point of the limb is not firmly secured; and at the loosening of the ligament by chance escapes the spur, and repairs the work, and many times it happens that they grow without any loosening, and I desire it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	As for the loosening which is done too carelessly, I have often observed that it causes the weakening of the entire thread of hair; for the forces tear just as well from above as from below.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is equal all around in its entirety, but that the thread is well stretched around the skin; and that the manner of the first work be that you make the child think that you are doing nothing, if he understands, that you do not make him force the thread around the limb only lightly, but that you do it joyously in all the ways that you can; then you do it straight between your hands, and put the forces between your hands or take hold of your fingers so that the child does not see them, neither any instruments; then bring your hand to the limb and breathe or cough, and draw it up as high as the head of the limb; then fix it well with the dirt that is gathered, then bind the limb with a double thread, and bind it from one end to the other with another thread; and hold two fingers by the second loop to the pouch and the must index, and press between the two threads, then release the cough gently and draw the chief of the limb; then leave the blood to flow out naturally, because that is the cure; and put powder on and over the powder I drape a bandage glued with a piece of egg white soaked in rosewater, confirmed with rose oil and vinegar, and leave it on until the other side is healed, and cure from the other side until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the juncture is like this: the two thumbs should be tense and bent, and the fingers as long as the thumb equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundane if it is when the nails are forced at the incision; therefore it is fitting that you extend your nail, even though it makes an incision; and grasp it equally, and if you do not wish to keep your nail, if you hold it, and then grasp it.</p>
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If they trespass two days, and that which is beside the edge is swollen, if you leave it as long as the swelling subsides, and scorch it gently; if you grasp it as you wish, and hold on to the edge of the verge, it will do you neither good nor harm.</p
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the limb of things soured with wound of powder, which we have said or treated with powders, and if we grasp too tightly, it will go down, if it does not already; cure then, as we have said, until it is healed.</p
dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is if there is an obstruction of the stone, or blood clot, or bowel, or bladder stone, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine is not freed, and you see that the obstruction is caused by the stone which is in the kidney or the outlet of the bladder, if it is possible, let the patient bend his knees; and let him put his feet on the back, extend his abdomen from the part below his back, and restrain the patient as much as he can; and then constrain the outlet of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is freed; and if it does not come, as we have mentioned, and the patient feels great pain, if it is possible, let you administer extraction with all the instruments which are called “syringes”; and this is the form: either of hammered silver legier weight like a goose feather; or the caine of a long palm half, or legier.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus it is done with a double thread, and one end is bound to the head of the bladder or to a wad, and the other end is put into the syringe; and the excess of the thread is cut off at the head of the syringe, then the syringe is closed with oil or grease and egg-white, and the patient is made to sit on the edge of the chair; and the bladder is raised up and the belly and the thighs are oiled with olive oil and tepid water; then the syringe is gently introduced into the belly as far as it reaches the root of the belly, and the belly is doubled up from under the buttocks; then the syringe is slowly withdrawn from the belly, and the patient feels the urine coming out until it reaches the empty state; and this is not done in any other order than that which leads or follows, because of that which is in front or behind. And when the urine has been drawn out, the thread is drawn out entirely, and the urine follows the thread, and the syringe is again introduced into the belly until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are bladder stones or blood in the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled, and you see urine and medicines distilling, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», and this is the shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three holes: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped so that the medicine can be held firmly in place, if we can manage to remove the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see the medicines slipping in the bladder, put the head of the sufferer in the moisture, and pull from the one who is ensnared; if you pull out the moisture from the sufferer, and then push strongly from the one who is ensnared; if the moisture enters the sufferer, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle cluster which we clusterize the bladder: if it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from the armpit to the elbow, there are one or two holes; then take a bladder of a sheep and put the moisture that you see clustering the bladder inside, and tie between the two armpits with a double thread, and burn one half of that moisture on the fire; then put the head of the cluster back in the arm, and strain your hand over the bladder until all the moisture has drained out, as long as the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, if you take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it round; then tie the thread firmly through these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a ball, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie in the instrument; and do as you would if you were making a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	de la piere
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the previous section the methods of extracting stones, and the medicines used for this; and we mentioned the difference between a stone that has been embedded for a long time and one that is new, and the signs of each; and when a stone of what size must be opened in the bladder, in the uterus, and in the testicles; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is embedded in the bladder is often associated with an increase in urine, and this is a sign that the stone has burst from the bladder as if from its subtlety; and there is frequent hazing, and the patient complains of severe pain in his loin, and he urinates many times, and then becomes pale; and with these spasms the foundation is loosened; and it is light to cure the spasms until they have been going on for three years, and is more difficult in old people, and is like for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, first purify the patient with a laxative to drive out all the evil from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never happens that we can examine the stone without causing damage.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the limbs, loosen and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; and let it go without force at any height; then make him sit between your hands as if in prayer, and let his hands rest on his thighs, so that the bladder is completely empty; then inquire and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten to cut above the stone immediately
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not yield to the toucher, take a little oil from the left hand, if the patient is elderly, or from the middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; and put it on the foundation, inquire about the stone, and when you feel it in your middle finger, if the bladder is full; then press on your middle finger, and the stone will come out or you will see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand the testicles upwards, and his left hand to grasp the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the size is taken; then insert the sponge covering, as it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And between these two that are between the shoulder blades and the foundation, do not put it in the middle but at the cost of the left armpit; and be right above the bone, and two below either the bone or foundation, and be the size that will traverse if it is wide by default, and within narrow, according to the quantity of the bone, do not make it too large; for by chance the press if it must be on the bone or foundation, that it leaps forward in the work; and that there are incisions that are part of the bone or that have angles, and margins: if it is gripped to tighten; and if there is part that is swollen, it is like a gland, rounded, from which is issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And thus if there are angles and margins, make the size greater; and if it does not leap, it is certain that you must pull on the tendons which are just like a file at the head, for the muscle is to pull the bone if it does not escape; or you can grasp with the instrument that is curved at the head; and if you do not manage to engage it, if it is too wide, or if the bone is not decorticated, if the straining of the vitriol; and if there are several bones, pull out the greatest at the neck of the bladder first, then follow above, then the big one, and the small ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is large, if you cover it with silk, it makes a greater wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And if it is large, if you cover it with silk, it makes a greater wound. For in this case two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes to an end because his legs cannot support him; but whatever you do to stop this, or to remove the nails, as long as you tear it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, if you apply incense and aloe and dragon’s blood, and bind it, and put upon it a wet cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up on his chest and do not loosen the ligature until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have pulled it out, if there is much blood oozing from the wound, then treat with lard of olive oil and vinegar, and with lard of beeswax, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if blood clots come into the wound and corruptions, and congestion of blood in the bladder, and either because of that the urine is retained, which is known in part as without jumping with the urine: drink therefore your dose in the wound, and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and bring it forth; then raise the wound with water and ease and oil, and support it in all the ways you know, until it is healed; and know that all the times you cure it, tie the two edges together, and unite the medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small, and it is at the end of the bone, and it is fixed, and the urine cannot pass; if the doctor of this whom I have said does not listen, then you must hear of the size for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this to be true
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one fourth of an iron bar according to this form and make two angles fixed in one handle.</start_of_turn>
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the bone below the stone, so that it does not come out into the bladder; then pull the thread gently until it reaches the stone; and turn the thread around the stone and the bone, as much as you can until you can see the stone from the other side; if the urine comes out then, press your hand on what is remaining of the stone which is inside the bone
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken, and spurts with the urine, and is stained with the patient’s blood; and if you do not know how to do this by any means, then take a thread from below the stone and another above, and pull the bone straight over the stone between the two lines, then pull it out forcefully, and loosen the thread, and apply cold to the wound; and the doctor until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the bone at one end and another at the top; then bend the limb so that the bone is between the two joints, and pull it out forcefully, loosen the ligament, and massage the blood clot that is in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.</p
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is loosened in women, and this does not happen often, it is a good sign, and is defended by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-versed in matters of love, even among the most learned.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	If by chance one cannot find a woman who is well learned in this art of hands; and if the woman's thumb is thicker than the man's thumb, for it can make a deeper cut, and greater fear has it. And if necessary, since this is the case, if one takes a small needle knowing well where to pierce, and with the thumb one grasps the root, and if one does not find it, not even with the most subtle inquiry; and she presents a fool in life, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and commands her to do what one commands of her by inquiry of the thumb; and look well if the woman is a virgin: for then she must push out her navel or foundation and question the thumb; and if she finds it, if she constrain her navel with her left hand, and recommends that she hold her navel or with the patient, and wants and presses her left hand on her belly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If the stone lies within the belly from the entrance of the bladder to the root of the thigh, then grasp the stone in the root of the thigh and find the navel which is usually hidden there, and feel the stone in that place. Do not move the stone up or down, but keep it at a small size. Then gradually enlarge it, until you feel the stone so tighten the wound as much as the stone can bear, and discharge the stones in various ways: small, large, sharp, smooth, long, and round, which are many times the cause of death.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if the stones resemble each other in appearance, it is known that they are discharged.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it does not go away, if you put vinegar broth in, and keep it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the stone is discharged, and have the instruments that I have told you about for extracting the stone as a helper in your work; and if it does not go away, and it is the artery that is cut, if you put powder on the wound and strain with bands and pins, and do not do it again, and leave the stone alone, only by chance will the patient die; then cure the wound
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the colour of blood is calmed and the limbs are relaxed, if you return to your work, as long as the wound is open.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as dense as lead and as hard as stones, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it truly in the belly of the egg, if we take care that this is not another exercise; and it is the skin of the stone between the white fat that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramus is of weakness that comes from the stones, and is spread throughout that matter
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never if percussion comes upon the bones, and this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or it is black, or aquous blank, and this is more; and these are the signs of corruption of this assembly, for if it is white or yellow as we have said, if there is swelling, the bones are long as if in the figure of an owl, and they do not open, because there is moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh, if there is swelling with a part of the bone, and because of this it is thought that it is another owl; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the white substance, if you feel well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it shows throughout the whole surrounding area, that is how it appears.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which comes after the introduction, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we draw out the wound by fire, if it be known that the patient is well according to his power and the swelling of his body; then we place the hand above his shoulder on something high, and put on him a cloth of drape; then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right, and stretch out his arm to the second rib below the nipples; then we take the sponge and burn the skin of the nipples among those of the navel, and cut the skin of the nipples straight down to the white line; and we burn it subtly as he pleases; then we pierce the white line with a needle at one large hole, and drain out all the liquid, and then put in our sponges, and stretch out the white line; and do not touch the nipples, but only the white line; burn all or in pieces immediately the cost of him subtly, for if you do not burn it well it will return the liquid; and if the urine spurts out from your work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the work of the white line. Then assemble the two leaves of the shoulder at a suture, and cure it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the liquid corrupted by another disease, if you must tie the veins that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then grasp the bone throughout the suspension, drain the liquid, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if it is acute and assembled into two parts together, its quernions are two roots; if it swells the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound a layer of soft linen soaked in rose oil; and put over it another layer of wool soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two nails, and put under doubled cloths, and bind it up as it is said above.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool yarn as described above and sew them together at the groin; and one of the nails grasps on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the painful part; and the other two nails on the two angles, and when they are all assembled, the restriction is in the loop of the groin; and never is medicine permitted in this burn except for the size of a nail; and take one burn from the cultella, and prick the skin of the nails, and if it is as we have said, if the white spot that contains the blood is discovered; if you take the burn as described above, and pierce that spot as we have uncoined, and burn it with this subtle burn.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And so be attentive in all ways that you can, until you have plucked them out entirely; and keep that fire away from the egg; and pluck that it is more salve; and make sure that you keep the wound clean, and more merciful than the work of size; and if anything hinders you, or if there is suspicion of suppuration or other thing, if you can cure what hinders you, according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if you fear perforation, as I have said, and when you are certain by the signs that we have said that the aqueous humor is limpid, if you make the patient sit on a low stool; for pierce the abscess at the lowest part with a large needle, and make the perforation long and deep; and let the blood flow freely; then put a sponge on the wound and bind it, and leave to drain the remaining blood, and cure until the wound is healed; and if the white bile does not leave the wound, if you can drink a penny or the instrument with which the hydropic humor is treated, as it is said before; and widen the wound and make sure the blood returns, and reassemble after six months or when the wound has healed, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will recover his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the bites of the coccyx
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	The hairs that are on the root of this limb are in doubt and fear in many places, for it seems to me that it is better to leave them alone; and I shall tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that in the case of abscesses, both come from the bone, and I have seen many cases.</start_of_turn
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by excessive swelling and pain, which is spread over the joints, or by percussion; and the colour of the abscess is like that of old cheese; and there is no pain, but it is painful; and sometimes there is one abscess that is rough and bloody, and yellow in colour, and does not come from any artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from an artery, if it is known by the disposition of the abscess above, when you touch it; and it must not be touched by you
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition to express with a touch of the two thumbs, and may well make the size above this semblance, and above the other parts; and that you must take courage like a coion, then the egg is high, and the thread is white syfac, and deliver the suspender from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already soiled with these hairs, if you must indeed treat the egg, and you must take courage; and if it is near the syfac, or in what is within the vessels, if you must deliver all that is within, and round the cope.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the marrow is coming out from the bone or the heel, if you must cover it all, remove the yolk, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the work is done, if you are treating a wound, smear the wound with coarse wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then apply other remedies until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	from the bites of the coccyx
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering resembling a bladder, with the softening of the coions, and the patient groans when it goes; and the cure for this disease is well near as poor as this one we have just mentioned, and all these things that we have said about it, according to what the ancients have done
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on the edge of the bed, then suspend the gown from the hooks at your two shoulders, at all the vessels that are protruding from the waist, and grasp the master of them, and extend them forth; then cut through the tough membrane wide through to pierce the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then pull back cautiously, as we have said in the extraction of arteries from the temples; then insert a needle or there is double thread, and bind it to the first root or the place where the vein has come away, and bind it loosely to the other root; then cut close to the middle directly, according to the length of the bone, and in passing the corrupted moisture; then cure the wound as with the others or apply a bandage, so that no vessel is left that does not nourish one of the hooks; for by that there will be no harm, and if all the vessels come together, it is enough to pull out the hooks to all the vessels; if the patient does not lose his nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and if they dry and do not swell.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface of the skin
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	When the fruit of this radix appears by section from the navel or from the extension on the belly in the flank of the spleen, because the intestine descends from that passage to one of the ribs; and this passage is either by incision of the navel or by the extension of the spleen, and these two methods of occurrence are caused by: percussion, or jumping, or pulling, or pushing, or the elevation of grief. And in like manner. And the sign that this is an extension of the spleen is that there is some pain and some pushing in the loin, and it does not come immediately; and the spleen is equal in size up to the navel, because the spleen presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the scapula is fractured, that it immediately causes severe pain, and the scapula is displaced, from the stretching of the skin and the bursting of the bowels.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never does the marrow go out with the intestines, and is retained as it is, and causes great suffering to the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of fire with fear, for it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	When you are commanded or the patient orders that the intestine be returned to its place in the wound if it can reenter; then either sew on his collar between your hands, and hold the flanks; then turn the thumb upwards, and cut all the skin of the ribs along; then go inwards from the liver, as large as a bean, according to what you must do to open the wound. And do as much as you must. Then pull out the spleen that is beyond the skin of the ribs, until the white spleen is discovered from all sides; then put your index finger into that which teaches the rib, in that which is between the white spleen which is beyond the skin of the egg, and between the second spleen, and withdraw that which is behind the egg, and between the second spleen; and thus move the thumb of the right hand inwards towards the ribs, and place the white spleen at the top of your left hand, and keep the egg towards all the spleens; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and unhook that which is behind the ligament; and ask if there is any intestine or white spleen left around, and if you find nothing, if the wound is at the bottom; then take a needle or make a large thread of X threads, and pass it in the back part of the spleen, which is after the skin of the ribs; after the size, then cut the threads that appear from the needle, until there are three threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and tie the spleen, of which we have said that it is beyond the skin of the ribs, with a strong thread of two parts; then cover the threads with the skin, and tie them in two parts, so that no blood vessels that are nourishing it can enter, except for the vein that comes from the navel; and remove the thread according to the first thread along two fingers of that which is at the beginning; and after these two threads leave the spleen that is beyond the thumb of the ribs with the greatest part of a finger; and after all the rest according to the roundness of the egg; then cut in the part that is beyond the skin of the ribs, as much as without error, and bow as we have said before; then apply a dressing of fine wool in oil, and put it in the wound, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is the fat cauterized beyond what we have said, after the incision, due to the fear of bloodletting.</start_of_turn>
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this work, there is often the evacuation of blood, and the leaving of the limb as long as it bleeds; and if it lingers too long, if it is raised from hot water, put on that which we have said, until it bleeds; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this matter, I have never seen anyone who could cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancient ones said that it is done like the bark of a tree that binds the screw, in such a manner that you tie the veins, after the size above lightly downwards; then hold firm, and cure the abscess of what causes it, until the veins cease to bleed; and cure as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes blood comes out violently, as we have said, and opens the wound; and do not take out any intestines as companions, and if there are any, that is bad, and repair them at once; and all the while if it stays too long in this place, if the wound or swelling is believed, until the intestines are taken out; and this happens from the stretching of the sinew which is in the groin, as we have said, because it is taut, then it is softened and loosened the wound and open; and it is cured as we have said before. And never is it cured with iron in this manner: and that the patient lies groaning on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the dislocation and enfold it widely according to the quantity of three fingers; and then draw out the sinew which is from the skin that covers it, and take out the nail and put out the limb appearing from the sinew; and press at the bottom of the belly, then cut out the two nails appearing from the sinew on the top of the nail; and cut one and the other; then draw out the nail from the nail, and do not cover the sinew or stretch out the heel or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the sinew of the intestines; and then cure by the cure of the wound.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you have closed the wound, if the swelling subsides and heals the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The surface is contracted, and shows no mark in the course of treatment, and the cautery is useless in this location, and the surrounding parts are more susceptible to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the nails of the house are softened in lukewarm water, for the nails that are within are softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to scrape off the softened leather on the natural leather; then assemble the layers one over the other with a seam, and if you see that, close the first excess of softened leather with two or three stitches firmly; then scrape between the stitches and cure as the other wounds, until they are healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	The wounds that are scraped off in our law, and for this reason I would not speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to force them except in two cases: one is that the witness of the wound testifies when required, and the other, because we often see the companion of beasts of burden for our assistants, as with oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts.</start_of_turn>
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that scrapes are made in two ways: by traction or by incision.</start_of_turn>
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the traction method, make the patient sit in warm water, until the wound is softened and painless; then grasp the hair with your hand, until it is set and you no longer feel it.</start_of_turn
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the armpit: command that you keep the best hand steady, and press the skin of the armpits towards your left hand, then bind the bandage, and hold each stitch at I stitch, when you have well secured them; and leave no trace of blood or superfluous blood that is outside the vessels; and this method of cautery is milder than that which is done by traction, because by traction the hair remains fixed by chance; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Saiches that chastening is commanded in our laws, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary to do so for two reasons: the first is that the patient will respond when asked in the saige; and the second, because we have often had to cauterise beasts for our attendants, as with oxen and sheep and goats and other beasts. I say therefore that chastening is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.  In the one that we do by traction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the hairs are softened and pliant; then we grasp them with our hand, until they are set and you no longer feel them.  Of the size of the chastening: it is necessary that you hold the beast, and press the skin of the hairs with your left hand, then bind the suspenders, and grasp each heel with one hand, as when you have well supported them; and leave no wound or any secret wound that is outside the vessels; and this method of chastening is milder than that which is done by traction, because at traction remains by chance no part of the hairs, by which the beast desires to loosen.  Then cure the wound until it is healed.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways like these: one if between the two testicles there appears as much as the figure of nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in childbirth it lets out urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has on the genitals as much as a penis and two testicles
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And as for the treatment of wounds and burns, if you manage to cauter all the boils that arise, and treat them like other wounds; in the second method, for those who urinate through the navel, if there is no other remedy.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as in homes: one if between the two testicles opens as with the figure of the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the court it urinates. And the other manner if it is in women, and has upon the navel as a beard and two testicles. And the cure of the womb and fame if it is that you cut out all the seminal vessels, and the cure if like other wounds; in the second manner, of homes whose urine leaps through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The fire cautery is applied above the natural parts, as long as it is too painful to see; and many women have as much with their hand as with a man, and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to hold the excessive movement of the hand or wrist and cauterize gently; and do not push too deeply, for blood will flow out, then the wound must be treated as any other wound until it is healed; and there is another burn that arises from the root of the tooth, and the pulp, and by chance it breaks through, and this is called the ancient "coward's disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you are certain that you have set it, as we have said, then hold it until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If the woman's nature is not fully understood, or if the rupture is slight; or if it comes from birth or by disease; or by a sudden injury, or by thick mucus or spittle, or by worms, or by injury in the marrow, or on the coasts, or in the bowels, or in the face; and if the conception is delayed, and the birth is difficult, or if there is an abundance of flowers, then knowledge of this is by experience of the dance.</start_of_turn>
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is close to the surface, whether on the thumb or the little finger.</start_of_turn
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is thick mucus and is close to two fingers, if you are in a hurry, take two fingers together and hold the woman behind her, spreading out her legs; then pull the two fingers forward as long as the thick mucus is round, and as it is over the swelling; then take hold, and pour oil over it, and put it on the limb, and lie the woman down with her chest against each shoulder, so that it does not swell again.</start_of_turn
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	If the scapula is hard and thick, it is best that you seize it with the thumb resembling a holly leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If stiffness is caused by bone marrow, if you suspend it at the hip and grasp; and have medicines that harden blood, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, and plenty of egg whites; then mix in a large dose of lard, so that the wound does not stick; and let it be long, and mix in some lint; then be cured of other cures until healed.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when marrow comes into the marrow space, if you cover it according to this manner, do not perform an incision.</start_of_turn>
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an inflamed abscess in the marrow space, do not touch fire.</start_of_turn
des emorroides	of emboli.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	Emoroids are openings of veins which, without treatment, are usually harmless; however, when they become old, they become swollen. As we have already mentioned in the previous chapter, the signs and symptoms of abscesses are similar to those of boils, and I shall now tell you of those which resolve with treatment. I say that abscesses and swellings, when they are pressed into the flesh without causing pain, can only be cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the root of the flesh can be felt, are those which can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary therefore that you place the patient in a cold house, then support the limb with your thumbs and index fingers, and press into its root, then sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then leave it for an hour, then put it in cold water; and if there is bleeding, make it sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then give it barley meal, and mix it with honey and ale, and make a poultice of it on his back
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it swells, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if that does not happen, if it causes a wound at the back and swelling; then take linen and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of elderberry with old wine, and apply it to the wound.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the abscess is resting, if you see that the wound is healing; and the one called "albathir" is red, and is like a dark hair, if you cover it as I have said above; then keep the wound healing.</start_of_turn
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually happen; and when they are old, they become tough. As we have said before in the division, the signs and symptoms are these which announce healing. I say that emboldened veins and those which are full in the marrow do not feel pain, except when they are cured by fire. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the thumb and hold the index finger at its root, then sprinkle on medicines which restrain blood, such as alum and dragons blood, and incense, and the like; then close her up an hour later, and put her in cold water; and if there is any remaining blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and elderberry and the like, and then drink barley flour, and mix it with honey and anise, and make a paste of it. And if it has clotted, that is good. If not, make her cough up phlegm at the back and put on a plaster. Then take linen and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her cough up. And when the abscess is quiet, if it is cured, the limb will regain its natural position as long as it is healthy; and the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a severe wound, if you cover it as I have said the tough one; and then it will be cured as long as it is healthy.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many methods of abscess come into the market, such as chancre and prickly abscess, herpes, stasis, fistula, hemorrhoids and burnt abscess, and other diseases that I mentioned in the division.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is fitting that I should depart in this treatment of the hot carbuncle that arises in the groin, which is not a common ailment but which resembles a boil; and if you are skilled in the art of healing, observe whether the carbuncle is already forming at the commencement of its emergence, and whether it is filled with heat and fever, and if it turns red when you see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not be in a hurry to pierce; but let the patient rest until the pain has subsided; then seat the patient on the edge of the seat, and place two small stools or a cushion under his hips, and support him on his back and join his limbs so that his thighs are spread out, and put his hands down by his knees, and bind them firmly with a bandage; then draw out the abscess towards the lower costal cartilage, and bring in the instrument from which we remove the root of the abscess; and it is fitting that when you bring in this instrument, that you should first feel the depth of the abscess, so that what enters with the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not injure the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is fitting to cover the depth of the abscess with a cloth, so that the instrument does not grieve; and it is fitting to put the horn of the instrument at the bottom, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.
