And when the abscess bursts, and we wash the hand with water, if the covering coves the head, at the navel; and when the belly is emptied, if you wish, put in the wound some soft rags soaked in rose oil, or in dry green oil; put the rag firmly at the bottom of the wound, and put over it a layer of coarse cloth and a layer of fine linen soaked in water or mallow which have been boiled; then cure after two days of washing following that, until it is healed; and never remove the dressing and the wound by clinking with water and honey, and then with water or angelica roots and alum.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is stitched in the belly, if you wish, that you take care not to burn it, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	De l’enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master first teaches at the play that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman press down on the navel, and desire to smell the afterbirth; then the child hastens to emerge immediately; then the afterbirth follows according to the natural figure, and comes out with the head, and the other hand follows her; and when you see these signs, if you press lightly on her belly, so that the child comes out stretched; for when he descends on his head, if the other hand follows him, and the master is overcome by the madness of his excesses. And this is not otherwise but comes from an unnatural cause.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes from his feet, or comes from the ribs or shoulders, or the hands, or comes on his belly, or even from the throat; and is converted by chance from his collar, and by other wicked figures; if the master is at the play that she is wise and discreet in these things, and avoids error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures that help her
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes out head first by natural birth, and the woman is groaning, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and arise her nature from oil or rue or fennel seed, and then bring her between her two legs the little cushion from which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and hold its nail as long as the moisture which is inside comes out; and take the woman's belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with a clenching of fennel seeds with sesame oil; then make her swallow and vomit violently, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if it is now expelled.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If the two hands come out violently, if you must, hold them lightly and gently; and if they will not go in, put the woman on a chair, and support her feet high; then pull out the chair under the earth, and hold her firmly, that she does not cry out; and if the hands will not go in, and the fetus is dead, if you grasp the hands at the shoulder which is above, you will deliver the child, and restore her equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child upon his feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon his feet, if you can push him up high; then twist him to and fro, until he is even; then take hold of his feet and stretch them to and fro.</start_of_turn>
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he cannot jump up to his knees, if the command is to grasp and make him cough, and he expels sperm; if he jumps up, God willing.</start_of_turn
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	If it is not forced too much, as we have said, if the bone is slightly bent and twisted, as long as it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For indeed it is easily broken.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not jump up as we have seen, say that you take muscle powder of elderberry, oil of poppy seed, gum mastic, and bruised everything in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and remove this discharge, then let her sit in hot water until the ribs are numb; and when she is softened from the heat, make her drink a decoction of marigold, and give her some, and leave her for an hour; then let her sit on the seat, then make her cough and strain her mouth and nose, and take hold of her belly lightly, for the child is now jumping.</start_of_turn
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the issue of the child on his knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if he puts his hands under his chin and under his jaw; then either he is overcome with sleep on his collar and his tongue hangs out, or he is senseless and rigid. He folds his hands under his chin and under his jaw, and then he grasps his hands under his belly, and he twists the cushion downwards until it appears in his throat; and if the child does not cough, he takes his tongue and moves it, then he moves his belly upwards, and he lets go of his hands. And the child is unconscious and limp; and command the woman to stay until the child comes to his senses.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	And thus the child cries and cries; and instructs the woman to hold her attention until the children are done.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I can teach you how to rejoin the limb: if it cannot be rejoined, if you make the woman rise up, and call for help; if she cannot call for help, if you make her sit on his lap, and she bites his legs; then mix in the muscle that I have told you of. And if she does not deliver, if you make her sit on the seat, then study to rejoin the limb; and when the limb is rejoined naturally, make her spit out, and command her to stay until the child comes to his senses.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the child upon his neck, and his hands spread wide, and his face turned towards his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I command that you grasp her hand firmly, then turn it back and forth; and when it is even, put upon the oily muscular substance of elevation and oil, as we have said, and then command her to move back and forth; and when you have done this, make her sit on the edge of the bed, and command her to brace herself; and she will vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	From this same measure at all the second time.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this method at all times, if the second toe touches your nail, while the moisture is expelled; if it swells up on her face and neck, if you press on the swelling, that it should not be retained, and the child will die; then pull the child out, as you have done, and command the woman not to touch her again: thus it will be gentle.</start_of_turn>
de l’issue des gemelz	When the dislocation is slightly loosened.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	When the swelling of the shoulder dislocates repeatedly, it is not strange, and often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is an unknown thing, and it does not live alone, if its name be known; I know that it is multiplied, and is dispersed by the substance which nourishes it, which is linked to the belly; and it never escapes as naturally as all the others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if it escapes cruelly, if the cure is as we have said, and if there is a subtle dance, and makes broth and makes lighter what it does; and make so that it is as if it were worth more to be saved than to be lost.
de plusors enfans	Furthermore.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are they formed in the marsh I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more, up to XV; and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of their glorious head, and it is fitting that the glorious dance should do everything, because by chance some things happen; do as it is fitting.</start_of_turn>
de l’enfant mort	From childhood until death.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure the woman of the dead child or belly, if as I have said in the division, and she does not come forth, and you are constrained by the work of your hands; if you believe that the woman is of sound mind and has no accident or fears of death; if you believe that the woman is lying on her back, and her shoulders are flexed forward and her legs raised; and you place your thumb on the second phalanx of her thumb or bind her to the bed if she is not being treated with the descending limb of the child; then wipe the mouth of the woman with a mixture of oil, alum, and fennel seeds and flaxseed; then anoint her hands with these oils and these mixtures; then bind them loosely in the basin; then want her to lie or make her lie down if she lies on her face; if she vomits in her eyes or in her nose or in her mouth or on her beard or in her hair or on her chest or on her feet, and if she vomits on her toes or on her heel or has loose bowels; and it is believed that she must hold the ointment at her dominant hand, and put her elbow between her two hands of the left hand, and hold her firmly with both hands, and put the ointment on none of these places that we have said, until it comes to the thing that is empty; and that is the form of the ointment.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then the doctor finds another ointment, or the third time he has to intervene, if the extraction is equal; and then extend them equally by moving from side to side, for movement itself, or by loosening the nails, if that is the way.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some remains stuck, if one feels some of his two nails slipping, and holds them in that part, and treats the other part; and if there is still some remaining, if you put this ointment or even higher up again, and do this until it is all gone.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be pulled back by the stretching, then you must cover over the drape, until it is whole; then pull at the toe or heel, and then you must do the same with the other hand, and have two thumbs.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	If the head of the shoulder is large and swollen at the junction, or if there is an accumulation of pain there, it is recommended to insert the thumb between the two bones and press down on the painful area; or to grasp it with the instrument called “almidach,” which is like the instruments or bandages which follow this; and in this way make the swelling naturally subside. Then force the bones apart, and if the dislocation does not yield, grasp it with force, whether it be fractured or not, until the moisture that is causing the swelling subsides. If it does not subside, break the bone into pieces at the fracture line.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	and if the swelling is on its side, if the attraction is slight, and the approach to the mouth of the marrow is slight.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is swollen in the belly or the arm, grasp the swelling with a cloth wrapped around the limb; and press the belly or the arm until the moisture that is causing the swelling subsides. And if the other limb is rigid and the shoulder is dislocated, if the patient bites his hand with his teeth, treat it until the jaw is brought back to its normal position; then apply an ointment or two, and force them out; and if the jaw is retracted by a suture that has come loose, if it is not possible to pull it through, it is necessary to administer moist and fatty things; and administer poultices, and anoint with soft and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on the cost, put it even, if necessary remind what we said of the living child; and if it does not go, draw it out in pieces, and leave nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if necessary remind what we said above about the armpits that come up in the marrow; and if blood comes, if put in water to restrain, and remind other cures.</start_of_turn>
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom a child was born dead, then consulted with another concerning it, and refuted death in the other.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went for help, and I thought for a long time, and could not stop the bleeding.</start_of_turn>
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong compresses, and out came a bone, and after a few days another.</start_of_turn
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at mouth, for this belly has no bone.

I saw the wound, and with trembling hands, while the woman was well; and I saw the woman long tense and soft, and this was already a sign of weakness; and I have never read in this chapter anything other than that when the master finds a strange thing, he must ask for help.</start_of_turn
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of the pressure, which is to keep the book closed; and there are two returns as two fingers of two hands.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Whatever be the horns more subtle in their restriction, or made of ivory or boxwood; and the mouth of the fist I must open wide, and the margin of the teeth I must lengthen, and a palm and a half; and in between the two limbs there must be two cushions of this same fist, which must be closed in one and the other, half a palm long or more; and these two cushions must be placed in the mouth of the marrow to open when we turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter, is made of ivory or boxwood, as much as the nails; and has two thumbs two cushions, as you see, a palm long, and two wide; and when you see the marrow open with all the instruments, if you make the woman sit down and keep her knees bent and her legs over, then put the two cushions together in the marrow and hold the handle of the instrument between her thighs; then grasp the instrument with your hand as if you had made the nails even, according to the quantity you see the mouth of the marrow open, until the jaw makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very sharp, and their resemblance multiplies their danger; and when you behold them appear, the work hastens, and the higher you are in your home the greater is your quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not covet the instrument when you do not see it, for its necessity is not to be excused
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second toe is retained at birth, if you command the patient to retain its nail, and then make her expel it with force, and hold your hands to her mouth and nose; and if she jumps for that, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not work, if you take a pot and make a perforation or cut, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the patient, like calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are boiled or roasted in water over the fire; then put a caine or perforation in the pot, and the other end in the patient's mouth, and hold it until steam comes out of the patient's mouth; then make her expel, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is sprained,
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If she remains after this treatment and there is no other force, command her to moisten her left hand with oil of sesam or in almond paste, and then put it back in its place, and wish for the second time; and when she has found it, if she grasps and extends it forward and backward, so that the marrow does not splinter; but it must move slightly to and fro, and then treat her. If she comes and it disappears.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the marrow of the bone is loose, we have said the cure of extracting it, and fumigating with herbs; and if it is not of all that we have said, if you do not follow the treatment; but it must be known that what is at the mouth of the marrow, that you bind to the hip of the woman, then clip it with lard tetrafarmaçon; if she will go and return, and will come with force; but nevertheless, when she comes there will be a bad smell in the stomach and the head, and she will vomit the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is deemed necessary, then appropriate fumigations are useful in this case: neither of the ancients have proven the effectiveness of fumigation with rosemary and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which we fumigate the woman at the retention of urine and the secondine if it is necessary is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is seen like a dog, and put the head under the earth, and the large bones on the fire; and either the fumigations on the charcoal, and the soot until it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the solid foundation perceived, for they are stifled by a subtle stiffness: if you must force them to dance, and do not allow them to pluck even a sharp splinter, and keep the wound closed that they do not touch; then put on a coat of wine and oil, and then cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will not stay in place, put or draw in a weight of lead, and leave hands clasped, and be still until the swelling subsides.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Never again will this wound or abscess come to mind; if it covers itself: if it is cured, as we have said concerning the weight of lead.</start_of_turn>
de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from its foundation.</start_of_turn>
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that arise from the foundation are nodulations, and those that arise from below the foundation deviate, or in the space of two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when the nodulation is old, if it persists, and is accompanied by moisture, white blainch or subtle swelling, and never are these fistulas permanent; they are known by the fact that they cause vomiting or flatulence when the patient makes an egestion, and by chance in a leap.</start_of_turn
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and up to half of the thigh; and reach up to the joint of the hip, and up to the navel.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows of the fistula which persists at the root and does not pass: and it is only when you bite your thumb or root that a fine needle of spider or iron is introduced into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, if you attempt to drain with a fine needle, or I pull at a horsehair, as long as you feel the attempt or the pulling at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and there is no bleeding, no swelling, no wind, as we have said: such wounds that do not perforate; do not linger in curing.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is formed up to the bladder or the urethra, if in leaping the urine escapes and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the hip joint, if the attempt of the vein is up to the limb; if there is no twisting and the invention of pain, if it is that it has become adherent below, and there is no need for medicine or dressing with ointment; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except toil, and the vanity of fools who intercede.</start_of_turn
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is neither new nor old, hope of health comes by fire, as I have learned; and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and keep the legs stretched out until his knees are bent towards his belly; then make an attempt to draw, or to plunge if there is twisting, until you have grasped or the attempt comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it at the root of his foot, if you must bite your thumb, if you feel that the attempt has been perceived; or if there is swelling or you feel between your thumb and the great toe the flesh or bone, then grasp that it is natural; if not, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One cannot well heal any wound, but this is what happens often; and the help that is given for it is this: if the cautery is too subtle according to the size of the fistula, as it is said beforehand; and one should cover all around in the fistula, until it comes out from the root; and do this twice or three times, until you are certain that these worms that must be cauterized are burned, which are like a penne of oil; and then cure with soft compresses filling the wound, until the worms are expelled, and then cure with oiling the wound closed and bound
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is still sane, that is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is still sane, that is well; for if he attempts between [treatments], and does not pierce until he reaches the root which is or underlies, and between your thumb and your index finger put on a thick covering of hair or lint, and you will see the fistula at that which the covering will wrinkle; if you grasp the start of the fistula, and hold it firm before the attempt, and then burn with the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered, and will be cured. Then remove the hair or lint which seemed like a sparrow's feather, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he will not move, and the surgeon is between him and the work, if the fire cautery or the medicine is hot.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the burning of these hairs that grow, and the coagulation of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of soft swellings covered in burr or broken pieces, until the bones creak and the hair is burnt in the creaking; then cure the wound of oozing pus with a hard scab, and these are the dry medicines
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula arises up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if the bone or root is grasped or questioned concerning this.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If thou feel the urge, and between two thou art in the web of cloth or silk or hair, or it is near to pierce, if there be no other way but to go forward and hope, by the administration of one of these three methods: or thou cauterize it as we have said, or thou apply pressure until the blood stops, or if thou wilt thou make trial and cure as first; and do not go too far in your haste, that thou cover only that which holds the foundation, and let the blood drain in its natural course; then cure as we have said; by chance if thou art healed, or thou loosen that covering and the surrounding matter then that it is coped from the foundation, or by trial or by some pointed instrument; then confirm that hair which is in the wound, as thou wilt; then study to restore the wound and to close the fistula in the posterior part of the foundation: if it be a less grievous thing to the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs or tears out from the foundation of the leather beneath, if you take a bite pierced at the head in this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And indeed, if there is a thread of hair torn in two, and you bite through the attempt at the head throughout the fistula until it is at the root.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs or tears out from the foundation of the leather beneath, if you take a bite pierced at the head in this form: if it is grasped in the margin of the foundation downwards, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your head or foundation; and draw out the head of the thread, and gather the two ends together, and restrain one to the other, and leave it one or two; and do not restrain it any more, until the thread copes these hairs that are between the two, and which cause pain; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, if you force it to burst in all the ways you can, it will not be too much harm.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not be worthwhile making it burst by force if it is too deeply embedded, and then you must cure it as we have said, while it is still sound.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of a spatumile thorn whose fistula is made if it is moist and of one part and trenchant; and from the other part no, forasmuch as we must not cope with this, as you see here.
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Morbid swellings are of two kinds: either they are deep in the foundation, like grains of resin, and are small and large, and adhere to the surrounding healthy tissue; or if they are large, there are one or more of them, and they push out the foundation and the top of the foundation; but those which are pushed out have much moisture, and adhere to the surrounding tissue or to yellow bile or blood, and have a yellow color; and the cure for those which are deep in the foundation is for the patient to groan and strain to push them out as long as the foundation is flexible; and the thread will appear. If you are hasty and grasp them by the nail or hold them with your finger, then take hold of them at their roots; and if they are unable to hold them because of their moisture, if you tear them with a drapeil or cotton or a piece of chamoly, and draw them out, then cauterize them with the cautery as it is said or as the physician instructs; for the cure of other wounds as long as they are healthy. And if the foundation cannot recover, if you bite the patient with a biting and rough astringent plaster to uncover what is deep or the foundation, if it can recover openly; that is if the patient does not resist. And if the threads are flexible, if you grasp them by the nail or hold them with your finger, and then take hold of them, and cure them as we have said, as long as they are healthy, and that they fear the incision with a knife.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you wish to secure the suture according to this method: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through from below and pierce the needle through from the other side. Then draw up two threads from the needle, and if it is thick, strain the thread firmly. Then knot the thread, withdraw the needle, and secure all the others. Leave one loop to correct the excess blood; then put on the foundation a moist drape in rose oil or cerate, and put on the foundation. Command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it contracts. When it has contracted, if the wound is healed and other treatments have been completed, while it is still sane.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when it is dry or firm.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is advanced and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice that a scab has formed at the edge of a nail or at the root of your nail, which does not allow it to dry; then treat it until it is healed if it is possible. If it does not heal, if you must continue to scrape it more vigorously than before, until it is raw, and is bleeding; then treat it until it is healed
dou fremit	completely.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small creature that appears before the body, and goes out from the mouth; and never does it bite the true, and one feels as though it is dead from fear, and comes to all parts of the body, and more so than in other places.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And if you wish to cure it, take a goose quill or a strong vulture quill, and put that quill on the bite, until it circles the bite all around; then pull your hand back with all your might until you have caught the bite all around, and pull it out from the root, and scrape the bite from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that he does this with a needle or iron as it is said above, and be subtle and restrain his limbs:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see that he does this with a needle or iron as it is said above, and be subtle and restrain his limbs, do not make it obvious, for it must be kept secret, and press firmly.  And if you see that he does this, if it is before or during the cautery procedure.</start_of_turn>
de la forme dou clistere	de the form of a blister.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a blister with silver or gold, or with melted lead or mercury; and never make a blister with these small and large instruments, as they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in their children and infants are puny.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if it is excessive, or the belly is tied up in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is swelling or the belly is bound, if you see, and the shoulder is wrenched either pierced or cut; and on one side there are two holes, and on the other one there is one; and either the belly or the owner puts medicines inside a bladder or parchment, and either cut around all the holes, and put between each hole one must leave a space, then put in these holes one strong thread of thread twisted in the shape of an X or around; and assemble the belly as if it were a nail; and when the medicine is inside, if it has the instrument before a strong thread, then tighten; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let neither the medicine be too hot nor too cold; anoint the head with ointment of oil or egg yolk, or something similar; then bind it loosely. Then seize the hand of the minister with both hands together, until it is quite still, then draw out the ointment, and leave the patient with his legs exposed, and if the medicine sees that it suffices, if the patient sleeps all night, it is better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he has put it on in a state of sickness of swelling of the belly, and the physician wishes to depart, if he begins as soon as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is swelling or bruising, or an abscess, if the ointment is as subtle as for a young child; and this is the form of subtle ointment that is applied when the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the previous chapter the treatment of wounds; or rather, the treatment of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on what causes them, and depending on the limbs or parts of the body that are wounded, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are by biting of stone, and size of spear and nail, or lance or fist or sickle, or similar things; or that are made according to the custom of the land, as for example a wound that bites on the neck, or on the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for a wound of the head and will begin with simple wounds, for the memory will come back to you in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a bone is fractured, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that there is no spitting of stones or other things, and the skin is thoroughly ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt the wound itself: if you do it too soon after injury to the head, even if there is blood from the wound itself, or let the blood flow in the opposite direction to the part affected; and listen to the patient's complaints of swelling of the head and neck.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he does not recover, if he is apathetic to meat and does not drink wine, does not eat cheese; and remove the wound, if there is spitting from the wound, cover with moist lint in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no spitting from the wound, if the wound is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, or anything else, I will tell you about that later; and if it has been moved, put on some external dressing, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like a nail and some, and the layers do not gather together by tension, if you gather them together by stitches, as I shall say for wounds in the belly, of stitching
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by bone, and is raw, and only held by a little flesh, if the bone is grasped; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hair firmly in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat plenty of solid food, such as meat and bread, and fish, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you find or split skin that does not touch the bone, if you grasp the wound tightly, and tear out the pus, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without support cannot be staunched by medicines, if it is an artery, and if you find it dislocated, if you can join it with a thread; and if this does not help, if you cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a minor cure: then put on this powder which solidifies as soon as it has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind them all together; and apply them to the wound, and hold it firmly in place, until it heals well and joins together all its blood; and then bind it well and leave it to dry, if it does not swell; for we do not burn medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we do this chalice solely, when we have neither incense nor blood of dragons, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has moved from its place, even if it is still in its position, if no other remedy has been applied; put on some oily unguents or poultices made of flour of barley boiled in water and honey, until it has sweated profusely; then apply other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If a fracture accompanies the wound and is small, if the edges are slightly chipped; I will tell you about this later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If the nerves are involved, if there is no other remedy than to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restrictive, because it hinders the nerves and causes them to retract; do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of blood is with the brain, which is the most important limb; but if the medicine is strong, like chalice wine diluted in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and poppy seeds washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this method, and oily unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, and the edges are bent inwards, then hold it together until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the flesh is swollen and filled with pus, if the artery is cut, and blood flows freely; if the bone is fractured, and the marrow and the cautery mingle, if the wisdom tooth is cut out, or the tonsils, and the tongue is held back, because the meat will go down, if the tonsil lies upon the jaw, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural position; then strain it immediately, and leave it untouched for some days, then cure the wound with oil until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments are numerous, do not take out what you cannot; and leave as much as the wound will bear, and be freed and aligned at the issue. And if the wound is fresh, if powder is put on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the cure must be made as I have said in the chapter.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of from a wound of a lance or a knife</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, if you see that the wound is open to the wind, do not allow the patient to move; for the wound is mortal. If the wound is not deep and is fresh throughout, do not put powder in it at the first hour, but leave it open, and cover the patient. But put an atractive dressing on it, and bind it twice. If there is no bleeding, put in the wound some cotton to absorb the moisture, and make the patient rest on the wound for three days, or four or more; if there is no spasm, do not move the patient unnecessarily or cause him any distress. When you see the bones in their place, if the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tension of the tendons and other cures, as long as it is sane; and if it cannot be cured, and if it persists, remove the diseased parts that there is fistula; if the cure is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or knife, and is simple, or worse on the front or back, if the cure of that which is before; if it is large, suture; and if it is small, powder, and if it is embedded in the bone, and has broken pieces, if you want the wound to heal, and the edges to retract if they are loosened; and if they are not loosened, if you leave it to itself, if it aligns the extractions; and for other wounds, the judge will know as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Pain of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; of a great wound never the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, by which the intestines are introduced; and the suture is more painful, and never is worth as little as the small wound as the great, because it brings back the intestines more to the point than if they are not brought back bit by bit; for the intestines swell so much that they feel the pain, if they are brought back more to the point, and for this reason is better the smaller wound, for this reason we will recommend that the intestine be returned to its place as it was before the other two.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines is pushing forward, and if anything is grasped, it is to put it back in one of two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak the area somewhat: moisten a sponge or apply a wet drape only, or you may bathe in boiling water squinting and spitting and spiking, and raise the intestines as long as they are swollen; and do not make this movement restrictive, and be quiet that you do not cause them to burst.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if the intestines are moistened with water or are cooked and bad, because by this is the entrance to things made; and if it cannot enter, if make an opening the wound at the instrument to cope the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to make it quiet that the size, that we must not cut without great necessity, and this is the instrument for cutting: if it reaches the hipbone and comes out, get out of the way; and if this is done, make the shape.</start_of_turn
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines protrude, if you stop the bleeding in accordance with its natural form in its own place, you will have done well, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, if you order the patient to sit up and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put the head and shoulders higher than the lower parts, and also if the umbilical cord is in one of the two lower parts, put your hand over that which is higher. And thus you must order that which I have said concerning great and small wounds.</start_of_turn>
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put between your hands I minister soft which holds all the wound together; and gather the layers. This is the common way of stitching, and take a needle or more according to the quantity of the wound; and leave a space at the head of the wound I should say at a distance, and pierce the two holes of the leather with the two holes of the siphac, which is from the inside of the leather, as much as you make it pierce from that part, and gather the two heads of the siphac together; then strain a double thread around the needle at two parts, and gather the two holes of the wound together again, and then leave a space, and pierce another needle; and bind the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not cease doing this until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and coarse, for fine needles cop up all the flesh, and the too coarse if they do not penetrate well: for this reason they must be moderate; and do not force the needles too far from the flesh and leather, that they do not cop up and open the wound before the suture; and then gather the holes of the needles, that they do not bleed the patient at night, and put patches or bandages to the holes of the needles for the most part to keep them in place, and leave them as long as the wound is sutured; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there is only one needle or two of the second kind that is common, and that you gather the two holes of the leather and the two holes of the siphac together with one needle or there is one strong thread in the middle. And when you have pierced these things together three times together, remember the needle at the part or where you began, in the manner that you cut the threads; and leave a space between each suture the thickness of a little finger. This stitch is useful for a wound that has a horn or belly, which was injured by a knife, and was more than a palm of great, and was from intestines well two palms of great, and was in the middle of the belly.</start_of_turn>
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will restore the intestines when they have been gone for twenty-four hours, and the wound has been closed for fifteen days; and the patient recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	Then the patient thought he was going to die, and that was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any medicine, for I was in Italy where there was no medicine, no ointments; and I only put a compress on the wound twice a day, and I poured honey over it until it healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it from the underside up to the point where the right corner meets the left; when it has grasped the right corner, if the needle goes too deep or is pulled too tight or if you have passed the needle, and you make it pierce from the other side of the underside up to the point; and you understand this stitching if you stitch just like a leatherworker and leave once the hair has passed over once, and take it back again from the other side, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does with great care, if it is so, that it is done without any other, which assemble the two parts naturally, and apply one chief to the other chief, in this manner: pierce a needle or chief of the neighbouring bone, and pierce only that limb alone, and leave the two chief of the bone; then withdraw the needle, and pierce from the lower part until it reaches the centre, with two chief of the bone; then pierce each one from the lower part until it reaches the centre, with two other chief of the bone that are on the other side; and this is the perfect method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens does this by word alone, and no one testifies to it; we must sew the belly with two needles, or there is thread in the flesh; and we must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and it is said that when the gut has turned inwards, the stitching is more painful than other wounds of the belly.
