Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is thus like the judge of other wounds: when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestines and the cost, then put on the dressing powder, and if it has moved, do not put on any covering except what is present, until the wound has healed; then tighten the thread, and join the edges, and the edges of the wound; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed. If you have no medicine, put on nothing but a piece of cloth, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You need no other medicine in many situations where wounds are simple. If you doubt that the wound does not cause common suffering to the principal members, you must cover it with coarse linen soaked in warm oil of poppy or rose oil, and put it on the wound, and drain the abscesses. If there is pain or pus in the belly and this happens many times, if the clusters of black vomit appear, and even if the pus comes up to the intestines; pierce the abdomen and drain, and extract what is in the large intestines, for it is lighter to heal than the small intestines.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot recover when they are swollen, for this is due to the swelling of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and for the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the cartilage leaps from the wound, if you reset it backward just as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is yellowed and becomes black, if you know that you must ligate the black part, because there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the layers, and suspend the two heads of the shoulder from the part below the wound until the cartilage is extracted, and the wound is healed.
de la routure dou boueil	From the root of the bone.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore them in their places among the bones, because I have seen that one bone was swollen or pierced by a lance; and the wound was at the stomach and became filled and turned into an fistula, and in this it caused vomiting and diarrhea; I cured it as I could, and I did not cease to soften until it was healed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	When I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has any harm in his belly; and there is no point of harm, but there is delay in many arrangements, meals and drinks; and they say that whenever there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be ligated in parts: take tweezers and grasp the edges of the wound, and when the tweezers have passed over the mouth, if you put two fingers over the mouth, if it stretches its mouth over; and then pull the tooth, and this is kept if it cannot be loosened, and put another tweezers afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is fully closed; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief tears in the intestine, and there is no other nuisance to the patient, and it can be ligated with a fine silk thread which is cut from the intestine of a beast, in parts: take the chief of this thread of intestine that is quite white, and then tie at the chief of this thread one thread of fine silk twisted, and pass the thread through the needle, and close the intestine, and retain it in its place; and this method of ligation with tweezers is not fierce except in the case of an old wound and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even if it is in one of the large intestines, if there is no danger or discomfort, except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	From fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds that open on any wound or abscess, when they burst, if called universally 'fistula', and even when they are shut and bound.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	When a wound bursts, if it is universally called 'fistula', and is shut and bound, even if shut and bound, it is as if a bird's quill has been broken; sometimes clear and low, sometimes thick and high; sometimes little, sometimes much; sometimes not at all, sometimes a little; and I have already spoken of this concerning the treatment of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no swelling, is due to one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or its hardness; or by its malice; or because there is a hard swelling within and on the lips, which does not allow new swelling to arise; or there is too much binding; or the flesh is relaxed, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in treating; or because corruption proceeds from pestilence; or because the property of the area is late in digestion and in healing, and flees by nature; or there is a vein or bone involved. And I have already mentioned these causes, their signs, and their treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you must know that I will tell you the cure of fistula which is made by the sweat of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Hairs that have become inflamed have occurred in all limbs with pain; for there are fistulas which arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the jaw, or intestines, or bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine, or at any joint of the hands or feet; and if they arise from the principal part of the limb, and there are similar symptoms.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All the fistulas of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is no fistula which does not reach its source except as I have said, you must give up hope of cure, and know that it will not go away; and if the fistula is straight, if you can reach the source with a needle or iron, and if the fistula is twisted, if you can make a small incision at the root of the twisting, because the tissue there becomes soft; and if the fistula is wide open and you do not know how to close it by stitching, if you can bind it up with one of the edges, because the moisture is short from one edge to the other, and it softens.  Then if you know truly the source of the fistula, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any other part which I have mentioned, if you must amputate the diseased limb according to what I have said, and remove the corrupt bones and tissues that are inside; and then the cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply rooted in the right place, if you can amputate as I have said, then put in stitches of fine thread up to the root of the fistula, until the medicine has eaten away the superfluous matter which remains at the bottom; and then put on dressings that will absorb the discharge until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as I have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, if you must amputate.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or principal nerves are swollen or bruised, or if the bone is fractured, and there is corruption and blackness, if the latter extends as long as the corruption embraces the whole bone, then hold the limb steady until the corruption is gone; and if it is not gone, and the swelling persists as before, remove the nails that hold you back until you reach the marrow; uncover and twist as much as you can until the corruption is gone, then restore the limb; and if it is finally sane, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If that is not the case, remove the nails too deeply; do not attempt to do anything further; if there is no other remedy but to leave it to its natural course; and if there is a small bone that is corrupt, and you wish to remove it, grasp it with tenacles, if the instrument is appropriate for that; and if there is a large bone, grasp it firmly, do not leave a splinter; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no risk of danger or fear, combine and support and release the bones.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you do not remove them at an opportune hour, if you place something on the wound that decays, and leave it until the wound is swollen around the bones, then it will become easier to move the bones. And if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, withdraw the swelling so much that the marrow is entirely exposed; then restore the wound. And if there is a great part of the bone that has decayed, and blood comes up to the bone; if you cover it with a bandage and cover everything up to the decay, and then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There once was a young man about thirty years of age who had a pain in his leg due to something within the bone, until the matter came to the leg, and he fled from a large abscess that appeared without any cause; but he grew mad with fear of opening it. However, when they opened it, they found that there was a great deal of matter in the abscess that became a fistula, and there was a great discharge of blood and moisture from the bone; and they continued to treat it for two years, but there was no healing in the art of medicine, as I was told, until I left. And when I went back to see the limb and the medicines that were being used, I saw that what was causing the pain was the large abscess. The bone became red and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I bound a thread in one of these holes, and then circled around all the holes, and found that one followed the other from all parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I thereupon bound one of the holes and found a part of the bone; it was corrupted and putrefied, and the corruption spread to the marrow; I removed that which appeared to be corrupted bone, and I thought there was no further corruption, except for what I had seen; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but I could not stop the bleeding; and then I began again, and I found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I soothed it, and then I stopped, and I mended the wound as well as I could. But as I bound round a palm of the bone, the marrow bled profusely, and I had to take away all but a little, and I restored it with medicines; and it healed and was bound up soundly, and there was no further risk of recurrence, except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear the pain, and for the fear of death which I had avoided for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is blood evacuated with this, but the patient remained entirely well; and thereupon, in place of the bone, there sprouted a hard scale, and it was in a good state and caused neither hindrance nor discomfort in any way, neither to the spirit nor to the body.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no place of pain, if you wish to sew it in this manner: take I thread, and strain it at the head of the bone that breaks, and command no one to extend it upwards; and put I another thread of linen thicker than the first, and bind it above the scale which is now departing from the bone, and stretch the head, if you tear the corrupt scale away, and uncover the scale above the place where you see it is sewn, that the thread does not break the scale; and put I a sponge or a piece of lead below the bone to cover the corrupt scale; and sew as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and sew again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open wide, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, if it reveals the marrow throughout; then put on a pair of gloves and with the forceps take out the corruption from one end to the other; and if the corruption is at the joint, if you break the corrupted joint, take out the bone which contains the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, if there is no other opening than that of the cover; and if the corruption is in the palm of the hand, or in the heel, if it is strong in that thing, but whatever it is, you must inquire about that corruption, how it opened; and soften it in every way you can, but that the vein or nerve does not prevent you; and that the incision and the sutures cover these bones many times, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of pus, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness. And for this reason it is necessary to appear somewhat familiar with the work of this instrument; and that the work will show you the instrument which you must use, according to your knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of diseases.
dou feu	according to what it is commanded, fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder may be dislocated by violence or by a sudden movement; and when you have treated that corrosion with medicines, it is of no use, if you do not cover that limb until the corrosion has ceased, for if the patient escapes by this means of death, or by the greater malice of the defect of the limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if it had been burnt by fire, and afterwards the blackness, for that corruption of the limb spreads throughout the limb and grasps all the bones; if you delay in covering it, and if that is caused by the percussion of venomous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and the like, if the corrosion is at the root of the tooth, if you do not stop it, it will not give the patient any rest until it reaches the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it reaches the hand, if the cope is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach the forearm; and if it reaches the forearm, if the cope is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death, and there is no remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and all that is done when the corrosion comes or goes. If it comes in the first joint, if the cope afterwards comes in the second joint; and if it comes or goes, if the cope takes all the flesh; and if it comes up to the thigh, if the cope is at the knee; and if it comes from the knee, there is nothing else that can save the patient but to amputate the limb. And you must bind the limb above and below, and stretch one minister over the lower link and another minister over the upper link, and you must uncover the flesh between the two links for one palm's width, until the bone is exposed; then you must cope or amputate, and put a bandage on the part that is bare, so that the bandage does not touch the sound flesh, and cause the patient further damage and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the limb too much, or if you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete. Then bind the limb securely with a strong ligature and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a case that happened to me: there was a black spot that seemed like fire on the bone, and that corrosion came first in the middle of the bone, until it consumed the whole bone; and when we saw the corrosion, if we covered the bone, it healed. But when the corrosion returned or came back to the hand, it happened again; I put on countermeasures after the softening of the abscess, but I could not stop the corrosion. Finally, I had to cut off the hand, and I did not dare hope to save the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off the hand, it would die, because the vital force of the body was weak. And he awoke and returned to his home, and when he covered his hand, it healed. And I have told you this case except for this one, in which we had to do something similar.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes an abscess in the limb that does not stay long; it makes great swelling. Then it breaks and bursts, and the swelling goes up like a vessel. The skin that is under is just as thin as a flag and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain," not "fistula"; but if it is so prolonged that it reaches the bone marrow, it is called "fistula." If the skin is split through to the very bottom, just as it is thin, like a flag, and is not corrupted.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you suspect that the skin is corrupted, but the swelling has not burst, and the skin is thick like hair, if the surgeon suspects a boil: look if the abscess is large and has a foul odor, then make a plaster of Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take beeswax, oil, and alum, equally, and mix them with the plaster until it is as thick as honey. Then take some of this plaster as needed, mix with water and alum, strain the abscess; leave the plaster in place for two hours, then remove it cautiously. Repeat this several times until the abscess is completely drained, and the pain is gone. Never use plain water for the abscess, only mix it with vinegar or wine vinegar. When you have done this, and you suspect the abscess is healed, if there is pus left in the cavity, take powdered diaphnet and mix it with oil of rose and wine; or mix it with other medicines or unguents, of which I have spoken before. If the hole of the abscess is small, and the cannula will not pass through, make a small incision with a needle, and put in a sponge of Egyptian cotton or basilicon, until it is enlarged. If the wound is too wide, if the thumb and index finger are left too tight, or if the hole of the abscess is below the level of the wound, leave only a little skin around the opening of the abscess.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the arm is broken, if you do not leave space for the bone to mend, and if you do not cover its bones as you see, if it appears in such a manner that the bone goes down lower than it is, for when the arm is broken, if you do not leave space for the bone to mend and if you do not cover its bones as you see, if it appears in part: that the bone goes gently forward, and does not leave anything of the bone; and take consolidating medicines to put out the fracture, and lay upon a cloth that covers the whole fracture; then put forces in the place where the bone was most broken, for there are often soft substances upon the other cloth according to the quantity of the break, and put the bone back onto the fracture line up with the bone, and do not tighten the great cloth too much until after once; and that which is outside the fracture, often breaks to put the bone back in place, and its marrow comes out from the bone, if it is venomous or putrid or enough, or digested or indigested; take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine has partially healed and you see the nature that jumps upon the fracture, if the marrow has already escaped, and approach the health; and then take off the dressing in the morning, or the third day, and when you take off the dressing, if there is any change in the swelling.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the wound bleeds profusely afterwards every day, soak the wound that the blood does not flow excessively.</start_of_turn
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison comes in small doses after a long stay, if you do not arouse me from my sleep, for the sickness is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if subtle poison comes in small doses after a long stay, if you do not arouse me from my sleep, for the sickness is approaching. For there are some who delay their meals in their wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if they lie improperly in bed after eating, their wounds do not heal. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the armpit.

Panarice is an abscess that arises from the swelling of a pouch of the hand, or of the foot, or by chance arises in other two; and when it is inflamed, and care is not taken, if it comes to a boil, it swells and bursts as much as it swells the root of the abscess, and by chance it swells all the way; and comes the corruption right up to the bone, so that there is sharp pain, and the head of the abscess is large, and the color is dark brown.

des vils	des vils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are large vessels enclosed with thick, melancholic fluid, which cause swelling in many limbs; more so in the legs of those who are prone to walking and working than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is appropriate to administer neither purge nor oil to the patient immediately, then the rest of the treatment.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	There are two methods for treating inflammation: the first is to apply pressure with a bandage and extract the black blood; the other method is to tie the vein and force it outwards.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first raise the affected limb high and warm for a moment, until the swelling subsides; then strain the limb of the patient from under the hip joint down to the knee; then cut the vein in one, two, or three places, of a large size, and clamp and extract the black blood from the hand, from the tip to the wrist, as much as the patient can tolerate; and then tie off the vein and order him to eat nourishing foods that will restore the black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do not harm the patient.</start_of_turn

The ailment of the limb is as follows: open the limb of the patient, if there is hair, then pluck or burn it out; and raise the limb high until it turns red, and swell the veins. And if you have no bath, if the limb is burnt with fire, then cover the part of the limb from the elbow to the knee, or from the ankle to the heel; then draw the skin taut, and loosen the limb from the socket, as much as it will open when you feel it; and you will see it red and black, and when it comes out or the skin seems like a white thread. Then draw out the hair from the root, as much as it will come out, and then put it back in lightly, and do it again in another place; and so on until you have done it three times. Then draw out the hair once more, or several times if you must; and leave it, and draw out the hair from the root, and do it once more on the other side; and draw out another size, or several if you must; and leave it, and draw out the hair from the root, and do it once more; and so on until it comes out whole. de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.</start_of_turn>

Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante. Therefore it is necessary to treat the vein promptly and continuously until it is healed and no trace of the clot remains. This vein has often been treated with five or ten fingers of lead, and in one instance, when it was treated with ten fingers of lead, one nail or perforation occurred, and the hole was made through to the end; and all the matter that was inside was evacuated, and healing medicines were administered without causing any further damage, and the wound was cured like an abscess.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow, or at the wrist, and there comes out blood spurting; cure it as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease," for it often causes the patient to spit blood, and is a small vein that arises between leather and flesh, and runs throughout the body, ascending and descending, and the patient feels it well in every limb as long as it breaks the skin or moves, and spurts blood; and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as bile, worms, and blood clots or tumors. And it is doubted of its malice, for when it runs through the body and reaches the head, it sometimes returns and destroys the marrow; and this often occurs.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture. This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in several members, and as it moves from member to member; and I saw that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis. Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel how it moves from limb to limb, because I have never known of such a disease like this before.

Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the scapula breaks through the covering of the pit, if there are little bones there; there is great pain, great swelling and great pain, and he sighs; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the spleen or stomach bursts open by chance, nothing of the indigestible meat escapes from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the spleen or stomach bursts open by chance, and by leaping out of the intestines nothing escapes from the wound, if there is no hope of recovery, do not attempt to extract the spleen.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the spleen bursts open in the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out in flow, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.</start_of_turn>
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if like the face and the throat and the chest and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine and the backbone and the thigh and the calf and the ankle, the limb mentioned above is subject to many conditions.</start_of_turn
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, because of this the patient makes another thing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There was once a pin that I pulled out of the root of a tooth: I grasped it, and it slipped from my hand the next moment, leaving the fat of the ear, and it was cured without any further treatment.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out a thorn from the fat of the oil from the marrow of the bone, and the thorn was replaced, and did not touch anything except the tip towards the ear; the thorn was as large as a Turkish bow, all in all quite painless; the game was cured, and there was no further mishap
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take out an arrow from the throat to a cresting, and the arrow was Arabian: I grasped the bristles, and pulled it out as long as I could, and the cresting was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And took out an arrow from the throat, which was hanging or swollen, and thought it would die; and when it had not passed for XXX days, and it did not mend; I cut on the arrow, and bound it, and pulled it out, without any mishap.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if the limb has an arrow stuck or lying inside, and the wound is deep; and left the arrow inside, and did not change its natural position, did not cause any discomfort in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And another man had an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was closed; and he continued to suffer great pain; and others said something similar
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And carry out an arrow at home of the king, that was stuck in mud near the knee, and was a declining inclination to the right side; and the arrow was entirely recovered. I came to the cure afterwards that it was stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very inflamed
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I would try to stretch it out entirely, and I did not feel it; and there was no swelling or pain on the right ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put on a wet compress that was astringent and digestive, so that the wound would not swell; and I saw the wound of the arrow come out
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the compress for many days, and I loosened the wound, and I kept the patient long tense, until he felt the arrow was gone from his knee; and he told me so
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put upon the wound the corrosive medicine by hand, while it was still raw, and held it, and felt the head of the arrow that had to depart from its place; then I closed the wound by that medicine, while the head of the arrow appeared to me visibly; and it healed well in the end of the second month, and then it grew so large that I could not keep my nails from being broken; and so I did not stop applying various methods of treatment, until I had made the nails well, as it is said at the end of this chapter, until I had finished with it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physicians say that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it nevertheless, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or tell me of the quality of the extraction of arrows, if you place your cure upon that which I do not say, for the books do not teach me all; but you know masters better than me about many great things, and about that which is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, descending from the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not arise from limbs or that they are fictious for it is not in this way: either by looseness or that they enter; or by another way. And that which leaps forth by pain or enters, is an arrow transfixed in the flesh, and leaps never again now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not leap now, if you leave it until the flesh is carried around, and is gladden the issue; and even if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot slip, if you leave it in for some days, and it moves every day; and then it leaps, and if it does not leap, if you pierce around at all that is subtle, until the flesh is swollen, and then you draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the splinter is lodged in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain, and there are no other accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: do not remove it immediately, but leave it until it is even again afterwards for several days, for if the splinter comes as far as the surface of the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the splinter is only lodged in the bone alone and does not go as far as the surface, and remains in the patient for several days without any other mishap, if the cause of removal is not known.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is not firmly fixed and cannot be extracted, if it has been embedded too deeply, as I have said; then treat the limb until it is healed
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the splinter is embedded in the bone so that it cannot be seen, if you attempt to remove it with all your might; and if you see it, if you attempt to remove it without any appropriate instrument; and if you are unable because of the wound or the depth of the splinter, and there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the opening is large; then remove the splinter if you can, and if there is anything in the splinter that holds it in place, if there is bone that is attached to two parts of the muscle that you must break or split, and break or split the ears of the splinter as much as you can until you can remove it; and take great care that you do not break the splinter, that you remove it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not do it once, if the limb remains bent even after you have pulled, then draw it out once more, for extraction is joyful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If blood flow contradicts the wound, if necessary, do what has been said in this chapter concerning its treatment; and guard against cutting the nerve or vein, and put in place as you would move the arrow without risk of further damage, either towards the head or the heel; and keep the patient still in the position in which the arrow was embedded, because that is the greatest aid. If you are unable to do this, follow the signs that it shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if there is no wound, or the skin is swollen in that place if we see it or feel it: then stretch it out until the teeth can grasp, and then extract it: if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, if you round your hand around it as much as it enters the bone, and dilate the bone, then extract it.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be grasped, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; if there is a lot of blood in the wound, if the bleeding continues, if the wound is deep, and you see that the arrow is bent, if it is grasped by the instrument, so that the tip of the arrow is between the teeth of the instrument; and then pull out the arrow, and if the arrow is grasped, if the instrument has a pointed handle entering the wound, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the bandage is surrounded, then you must grasp all the surrounding tissue or the venom is there; if so, then cure the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the bandage tears or breaks at the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and is close, and you must cover over it, if so; and hold the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the nails from which we treat the wounds are similar to the beak of an oyster, and thus is this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are various kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the wound
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape at the end of the shoulder is like that of a bird’s wing, to push the point of the bandage forward, as it is like this.</start_of_turn
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	its shape like pliers to grasp and pull out if it is thus shaped.
des voinnes dou cors communes	it is common.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins that one must know are about sixteen in number: two veins that are behind the ears, which are called "herbaces"; and two arteries that are in the temples; and two veins that are in the armpits, which are called "aspires"; and a vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and a vein that is at the back of the neck; and two tendons that are in the collarbone; and two veins that are in the cheeks, which are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.</start_of_turn
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins of the arm are four in number: one is the cephalic, and it runs on the inner side of the elbow; it is called the “chief vein.” The second is called the “fast,” and is made up of the cephalic and brachial veins; it is called the “brachial vein.” The third is either the right or left brachial, and it runs on the outer side of the elbow; it is called the “belly vein” and lies above the olecranon process.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The ulnar vein is between the radial and the ring finger; if there are two of them. In the leg and the foot there are three veins: one that runs along the inner side of the popliteal fossa, the second that runs along the outer side of the ankle; and the third that is called the “internal,” which is in the ankle on the outer side; there are three veins like these in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps as old catheter and to evacuate; and the quality of the physician, as I have said, is that he raises the head of the patient and rubs the arm or the veins are rough; then he tightens the patient's neck with a screw, while the two veins behind the ears depend on the head: when the thumb and index finger press on the side of the head, if there is swelling, then take the lancet and pierce the vein up to the bone, then keep the hand over the whole vein, and pull and stretch the skin and vein well together, and make the bleeding stop as much as you see; then strain and tie, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth an ancient emigration, soda, and obtalmia accustomed, and at the root of the tears there are drops; and the quality of the physician is such as I have said: and that the patient strains his neck, as the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse below his thumb, then he signs with his index finger; then he places his hand on the vein at the top of his thumb, and grasps the lancet below, and grasps the vein above, and the cope, as he has done in two other veins, and makes correction of the blood according to his need; then he releases the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts on a bandage; and then the swelling forms, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this in relation to its swelling and extraction, or its beginning in the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood of the front vein is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein for ancient fevers, for migraine, and for redness; and the quality is such that if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as the vein bursts, take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood of the front vein is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein for ancient fevers, for migraine, and for redness; and the quality is such that if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as the vein bursts, take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this. Place the point on the vein, and hold with your hand, or something else, and let blood issue according to the quantity you see; then deliver to the patient the neck, and tie the vein until it is whole and never let it be opened by a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Whatever, let the flames be too strong; and the same through, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are two fingers wide helps with the swelling, and with the tremor, and with the redness, and with the yellowness in the oil, and with ancient fevers; and the quality of their blood is such that if the patient strains his neck by twisting from any side, as before; then do the same, and either let the blood flow, for a long flame a wide flame, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make a drain of blood, as much as you are able, and then bind it up, and hold it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	When the blood of the vein is dark brown, and has a strong smell, and is caused by diseases of the face, as with measles and redness that comes on the face, and even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient stretches his neck, then strains his jaw to his left hand, and takes a long flame, and puts it on the liver between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily, and it is necessary to begin to correct it; do not go too quickly, but correct the blood according to your need, and leave it for one night, for it is usually restored by then; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two veins helps to loosen swelling, and to commence mixing, and to cure diseases, and to stop bleeding, and to dissolve tumors, and to remove herpes, and to stop stomach cramps; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient strains his neck from both sides, as we have said; and let the master be above the patient’s head, and the patient sit on one seat, then close the vein long enough, and take out the blood gently, or as much as is necessary; then do the same in the other vein, then remove the ligature, and remove any blood clots from the middle, so that the patient does not suffocate; and leave it like that until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the limbs above helps to cause collection in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and ulcers of the tongue, and pain and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And when you are to take the blood of the liver, you must hold the patient’s head forward towards you, and restrain his collar as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left side, and know them by their black colour, and that they have small black veins running into them: therefore close one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, if you see the greatest of the two parts from the back, and also do the two veins which are under and above, for this is a mean way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And of the blood of the veins of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins of the tongue helps after the cephalic blood, and it is at the widening of the throat, and there are diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and holds the tongue, and looks under each rib towards the costal margin of a black vein: close both of them, and do not take too much at a time, for there are arteries there.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins which we commonly use are usually healthy in two ways: either by puncturing with a sharp flame which is large and fierce, or by using an olive-twig which is subtle as cuts to trenches; this is called an 'anesil'. They are large and subtle according to the size and distance of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of the fire cautery is known to be mild and wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is a kind of surgeon who cuts open the large veins that are filled with obvious blood, which contain much blood and trouble; and this is the form of the olive-twig flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for safer veins, or where there is clear yellow blood.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basal vein, which is one of these veins, helps to cause diseases such as hoarseness, cough, pain in the throat, and swelling of the belly; and it is useful to know that it is accompanied by the artery that is beside it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If he grasps the flesh and blood flows, if it is to be held, as I have said; and do not be afraid of the flame, but cut as if with needles.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the vein does not open visibly, if you must extract it, and bind another; or you wish no blood to flow, or you leave the vein open at the arm: it will open visibly; and grasp the flame as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the blood vessel break, if you must therefore extract the limb, touch the part until you know its pulse; then sign the limb, and then bind the limb, grasp the vein with the flame; and beware that you do not injure the artery when you see the limb swell, for that is the artery: stop immediately.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see blood spurting upwards like the urine of a child, and it is pale and transparent, know that it is without an artery: hasten then, put your hand over the wound, and press your hand firmly until the bleeding stops; for this often happens.
