If the bleeding persists, bind the limb and leave it still, do not move the patient; and be cautious, do not move until the bleeding has ceased.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it is not stained, and it is painful, and the doctor is not present, if the artery bursts, because the head of the bone is pulled back; then hold it still without touching it.</start_of_turn>
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a bandage of physicicians, and make a loop, and take hold of one end and bind it well to the other; if it stops bleeding, that is enough; if not, if the wound persists, apply powders that stop bleeding; for the bleeding will not be greatly stained in many places by the little movement of the wound, and the power of the hand itself.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps to treat blood clots at the root of the head and at the root of the limbs, because it is composed of the basilar and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the patient to be aware of the nerve which is at the root of the limbs, and if it is not too deeply damaged, and if he finds the nerve, he inflates it and the blood is either clotted, and by chance cannot be cured; and this nerve is often torn many times, and if it does not open in some people because of its subtlety, it is necessary to take the blood from the anesthetic instrument and withdraw the nerve from its root.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it is too long.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein helps to treat blood clots at the root of the head and aids in the evacuation of the eyes; and it is necessary to cauterize with the olive or mirtle flame, for this is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Indeed, it is prudent to ask for the least painful method, and do not grieve if it does not work the first time; we start again. And by chance, it swells up for some people, which we cannot do the first time, but it does not grieve us.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thinking.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that if blood is drawn only for the purpose of preserving health and avoiding future illnesses; and let the blood be drawn from one of the three veins that are or should be: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the brachial; and it must be drawn at the commencement of prayer before meals, and after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and it must be drawn at the beginning or at the third hour, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood that is administered for illnesses has no fixed dose, but that whenever there is a need for blood or nourishment, in all hours and in all conditions; and it must not be drawn from children until they are twelve years old, nor from women for more than four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Must not be treated those who are older than sixty.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When anyone seems well, in whatever way, if it comes to guarding the intestines from a light distension, if there is much wind retained, so that the veins do not draw out the humors that are useful for the principal members; do not let him eat too much flesh or too many onions, neither too many fruits, as much as there is force in them; and if he becomes well again after a colic fit, vomiting and abdominal discomfort, and many times of belching, of going to the toilet, of sleeping and of lying down, and all that is good, or by some weapon or poison; then subtilize the humors, if they are not great, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you can; then put in or bathe, if nothing else hinders, to subtilize the blood, and keep him for a third from the vein of the wrist or the elbow, as we have said; and keep him engaged in work, in eating and in luxury, and in similar things; and bind and join, and make the patient sit higher than he was before, and wipe his arms twice or thrice, then pull out the thread from the middle, for if it is too tight or loose, it will not be able to correct it without; then wipe the wound with the hands, until the veins swell up, and are felt; then moisten the patient with a little oil, then place his left hand over that vein below the wound, and keep it there until he seems well again, that the vein does not swell and become painful.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins which flee like strings to the healer, and if there are some which are filled with windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it shrinks from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this; and if it opens the vein, it is the wound which is too wide, for because of this one must advise the healer in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, it is good; if not, if it recurs again, do another scar there or in the neighborhood, if the wound is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	If the limb is swollen and the patient groans, and leaves one or two fingers unmoving, do not enter or bathe, but restart the bleeding when it stops; if it has bled too much, or without due care and you doubt that there will be enough blood left to do what you see, if you are confident in that bleeding alone, with the flame quite upright; and the work is finished, even if the limb is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb inflamed, do not immediately renew the bleeding, and apply a pad of lint soaked in oil, for it softens the flesh of blood; and apply the oiled lint firmly to the wound to staunch the bleeding. This will cause a tingling and swelling of the limb when it is placed upon it; if it is too subtle, it will escape when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, even if it is not dangerous except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, if you are hasty, and put a wet sponge on the wound and a little charcoal powder, and hold it for an hour; and believe that you will have done enough after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in the limb after a few days no black or green mark appears, do not worry; and if you see it, do not put anything else on it, such as aloe or mastic gum, mustard, or the like.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Many times there is swelling and discharge at the root of the arm: put your hand there, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of your hand, that is an evil sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Listen well that you put nothing on it of what we have said, for by chance in court without an artery; but it makes it swell dry to harden the limb, then treat it with another treatment, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.</start_of_turn
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If it is black without, leave it black as long as it is red; if you see it large, leave it until it is slight; if it is too thick, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is advised for the one who is calm and strong, and has the mastery of bloodletting, to make the wound larger; let the flame be large; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and keep him safe and sound, and must keep him safe by cutting across, do not prick him. And this method of bleeding is useful for stopping excessive bleeding and preserving nerves, and is better than letting blood from a long distance rather than a large wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one who has a cold complexion, it is advised to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is faint, give him blood three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, give him soft bread soaked in honey, or aromatic honey with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant honey.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pricks at the blood after the evacuation of blood, if it comes to light that he burps up bile, and a fragrant vapor, and uses other things as we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If he sees his arm swelling up again, and gets better once, if it is swollen by a great amount of blood, he must rise up and rise up immediately, in proportion to the quantity of his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If he sees his arm swelling up again after the first bleeding, and it has become stiff, if he rises up three hours after the first bleeding, or after the twelfth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	If he sees his arm is better on the other side, if he must get better slowly over several days or weeks.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the belly which is already evacuated, and causes fever; if one can draw out a great quantity, and expand the opening as much as it bleeds; then that all the blood be evacuated, and put your hand over the pulse when it is well, that no more blood comes out in place of the vomit, and this often happens; and it is not good to draw out too much, for you may see the arm slip, and make the blood vomit again the second time, and the opening is closed, you must press firmly; if it is crooked, extend the arm as much as possible, for that would be bad; but leave it as it is until the second time; or you may touch the tip of the flame, until the one which is frozen at the opening of the vein has bled out all the blood in the vein, and put some water over it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not bind it tightly, as long as the incision is calm.</start_of_turn>
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to draw out blood the second time, if the same is in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.</start_of_turn
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The arm vein is bloody at the root because it is made up of many small veins.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And if the patient’s hand is grasped in warm water, until the blood vessel is red; then it must be bound moderately, so that the wound opens well; and then draw it out without great width or length; or make a large opening, and bring the blood vessel close to the wrist joint, and if it cannot be removed, grasp the hand in warm water again and leave the blood in the wound until enough; and if it is in this state, do not again grasp the hand in warm water, for more is put into it than in this state; and the blood of this vein is more useful than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salivary vein of the right hand is useful for all the diseases of the liver. This method is: strain the hand and immerse it in warm water, until the vein escapes if it is seen; and if it does not escape, and if you pull it out, and if you press it in every way, do not grieve; and do not press too much, for the nerves are all loosened from their sheath, and then grasp the hand in warm water again, if it is not frozen in the wound, and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if you put oil and lint on the wound to stop bleeding, and then make a dressing.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have said concerning the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is worth for all the maladies which are caused by the poison of the body, as well as maladies of the marrow, retention of flowers, disease of the spleen, and of the ulcers and the ancient legs, and similar maladies.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its blood is that if the patient has suffered with acute pain, and has rubbed over the belly until it swells, and has lain upon the joint of the limb; and if the belly is at the ankle, and from above the limb come out drops of urine; the blood is like that of a large rain, or more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you see the limb pale under the foot, if you are aware of nerves that are swollen, and the limb travels as if grasping; and let the flame be extinguished.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be cured, if you reset the limb in water, and let the vein discharge well.</start_of_turn
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	If the blood of the sophene must be drawn for the first time, if it is repeated a second time from below a little space, because the blood is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and do take the sophene of the other limb equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The limb of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its blood is worth as much as the pain of the hip, when it is for blood that is clotted.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient is between the heel and the knee, it pulls downwards from the ankle three fingers breadth; for otherwise it will not open the vein. And if it does open, do everything in every way you can, and through and through; it is better to leave it closed than to rupture it, for its bleeding is copious, and it is more likely to heal at home.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find that it has burst, if some drop of blood escapes or two, and towards the lesser side, and take care of the nerves; and do as much for the blood as you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it; it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	of bloodletting
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made from horns, or hair, or leather; and the application of the ventouse should be done in the following manner: either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting alone.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this bloodletting which is done by cutting has two methods: or it is with great heat, or with heat; and the bloodletting which is done by cutting and by extracting blood is done in twelve wounds of the flesh, of which one is at the top of the head; and the other is at the base of the neck; and two others in the two costal cartilages of the neck; and the bloodletting from the chin; and the bloodletting from the two shoulders; and the bloodletting on the hips; and the bloodletting from the two arms; and the bloodletting from the two legs; and the bloodletting from the two ankles; and the bloodletting does not treat any blood, except for the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not harm anyone, as we do when we do bloodletting; and it should only be administered, neither with great heat nor with cold, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as all the flesh is emptied.</start_of_turn>
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of disease commands it, or by custom, if the physician suspects a wound at the commencement of the month, or at its end, he must take his pulse and examine every tendon; for there are some who, when compelled to vomit, suffer great distress; and some who find swelling and redness in their face, in their head, and at the collarbone; and some who vomit blood in their mouth and have lost their tongue, and spit blood; and some who think they see blood and vomit and faint and die.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is covered in moisture like blood and sweat, we command them to be exposed for two hours after sunrise.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	When the physician has given the patient medicine, if it is of benefit for the headache … that comes from the vomiting, and it will not be of use before the evacuation of all the humors; and this vomiting is useful in place of cephalic blood, and is only of benefit to those who are pale in complexion or who have a cold sweat, because this causes them great discomfort; and for this reason it is not of use to them unless they have a cold disease.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if anyone suspects that they are becoming unwell, it is better to put on the suction cup a little lower down due to the risk of complications.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind coming from the head is in lieu of blood from the chief and bile, and for this reason it is worth at the expense of the stomach, and splitting of the channel of the windpipe, and all, and swelling; and it is necessary to push it out, because if it stays too firmly, it will obstruct the belly or the spleen or the liver.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind coming from the head is worth as much as the pains of the chief, and swelling and vomiting, and strangulation, and pain as the root of the teeth; and it is in lieu of the blood of the bile; and it is necessary that you command the patient to express his hand to put it there, that he does not compress the artery, and does not see blood flow outwards.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the south blow loud in the mouth if it is caused by a disease of the mouth, and by corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the cause of the health of the teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the south blow loud in the mouth if it is caused by heat and swelling
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind from the armpits is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it pulls blood from these large veins; and command the patient not to fill them up too much, because they are liable to burst, and knows of thorns and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	If there is a wound on the buttocks, it causes swelling at the root of the bone, and diseases of bones and nerves, and it is necessary that the dressing be large and firm, and that it adhere well; for if it is too loose, it will break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds of the legs swell widely, because they draw blood from all over the body, and cause ancient pains of the rains, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and swell the flowers; and are in place of the two buttocks, and the two ankles, and all of them gradually consume the body after a long time, and cause vomiting in various positions
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is as follows: if you apply it at first glance, and with steady pressure, and place it firmly, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see blood tinged with flesh and the redness of blood; then rejoice, and remove the suction cup, and take care of the body, for there are many who have suffered from excessive tension and clear pores: if you only cut once, you will make large wounds and a deep wound; do so gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If it is not large, if you must cut once, do so cautiously at first to dilate the blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If it is very thick, if you must cut three times; and when our wings draw blood, even a little, if we only cut once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins bleed excessively, if we rejoin them often; if their base is not firm, if we persevere too long, they will tear if the cause is not perceived immediately, and it will fall to those who have tough skin and hard bones, who have wide pores, that you must remove the stasis of the oily aperients and dissolvents: if it is in this case, violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of watermelon seed; and if it is in hay, fennel oil, or thyme, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	If the superfluous moisture is great and cold, take oil of marigold, or balsam, or oil of ivy, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If the skin is tender and there are wide pores, oil must not be put on, but it is allowed to wash after the evacuation of rosewater, or cold water, or black bile, or watermelon juice, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture in the mouth, if it easily rises, or of elderberry and sumac, and the like.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive discharges should rise from wine old, or from sea water, or from decoction of elderberry or chamomile, or from other similar things; and must not keep their ventouse before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and must not sleep after the venting, but must get up when it is time to vent and when it is vented.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And keep those who are cold shivering warm; if they do not, they are too cold and inflamed; if it is possible, let them take cold things, such as pomegranate seeds and radish and lettuce easily, and other things; and eat marrow, broth of barley, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, let them take honey syrup and scented wine middle, which is between old and new, and eat barley broth and fennel and small seeds and saffron; and when they have vented, they must drink more than eat; and it must be given to no one before or after the venting, in order to comfort the principal members; and be discreet about it, but do not let them drink anything else
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and under the kidney, and upon the belly and the buttocks and the groin and the heel, for in these parts the member does not suffer from any wound save for the purpose of drawing blood from one member to another, as we do when we place them upon the nipples when they do not bleed; to overcome the viscosity which is in the member, as we do when we place the sponges upon the belly and the buttocks to lighten the member; and to stop the pain, when there is swelling or a stone, for it possesses by its attractive virtue the power to draw out the swelling or to discharge the stone from its place; and thus it makes elevation when it is placed upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained moisture, and these sponges are administered empty without any liquid, and never are they administered together with fluid, and never are they plain with cold water, as in the case of pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the sponge with warm water or with water in which there are concomitant herbs that are suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the applied ventouse is like this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And he had two large and half palms of barley, or else a quarter of a league of mustard, as much as to push out an awl; and it may be of rind or wool in front so that it does not burn the patient when putting it on the limb. And in the middle there is a thorn of barley or iron, to put a bandage on, and there are great and small ones according to the ailments and the degree of those who take them; for the blisters of the sick are other than mere bumps, and leaner than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must place this bandage on the limb: grasp the bandage firmly or with linen, and put it through the thorn which is already in the bandage, so that it is taut either at the front of the bandage or that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and two must be placed either on the wound that we have said or on the mark that we have indicated, so that when we see it, if it is going to vapor, we must remove the bandage; and grasp the linen as before, and do it again often, if you are able.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	When the ventouse is used in the treatment of pleurisy, which is acute, there is no swelling or perforation, and it is only administered when it is filled with air, and is placed only on the affected limb; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	They are not administered for anything but limbs where it is not possible to place a ventouse because of their small size, such as the liver and teeth, and similar things; and in wounds stripped of flesh, such as thighs or lips, and other similar things; and the quality of the patient is such that when we find that the veins that are in soft, clean blood do not swell with the puncture, if they are taken; and we put in a plug of soft water, until they are full, and do not have anything in their bellies; and then either drain the vein and the ventouse, or scrub the limb until it is red, and put on the veins; and when they are full, and swell, if it is possible to put on the ventouse, we put it on, for it is better afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this does not suffice, if you lift the limb easily, then with water warm, moist well, and then express; and if the limb remains too long in the water, if you draw more than a cloth of linen in cold water, put upon it, until the limb is extended; and if the limb is multiplied, put upon it ground vitriole, or lead, and similar things, until it is extended; or you take out half of the hairs from the root, and leave them until they burn out on the limb, if you have finished now; and if you must do more, take other hair.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the hairs do not come out easily, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or you insert a needle into it until the hair comes out, and then put upon it, and as much as it feels blood, if it comes out; and when you see that it is biting, if you sprinkle upon it a little aloes and bruised sage, or charcoal, if it will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Ci comence li livre des brisures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear me, dear son, for in this book you will find nothing that former authors have ever written, neither in books nor letters; for this reason this science is strange in our land, for I have never learned of it from any other source. I know of it only through the ancient books, or through study and experience, or through the habit of my life; and I have described it in this chapter and summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments which are necessary, as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book are the sum of words and the chapters or the learned man puts his understanding into them, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proved learn and learn this noble art, and learn from others.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that whenever there is a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain, if you suspect that the patient is in need of healing on one side or the other, without any other cause, if there is weakness of the limb, or swelling, or old age; or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold; and if there is too much fat, such as cold baths, and oil of almonds and chamomile, and do not drink wine, do not eat greasy foods, and do not fill the belly too much with meat, until you are certain that the wound has healed, neither by excessive expansion of the matter in the limb.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, if you command that the patient be given no meat which makes great swelling, or which has viscosity, if it be like wheat flour in water, and rye, and testicles, and meat, and fat, and fish, and strong wine, and similar things.</start_of_turn
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in part of its nourishment, it returns muscle and more quickly breaks the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken by fractures and decrepitude cannot well reunite or knit according to their nature because of the drying of the limbs; for the same reason as those which are too tender, as bones of small children; but there is no remedy, remain above the fractured bone the great tensions which appeared and join the limb together, until it reinforces as it was before; and do not move from it, for because of this it is necessary to nourish with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And when there is some other method, it has its engine and its own instrument in restoring, according to what is remembered to come in its place; and it is known that the fracture of the bone is recognized by that which makes it twist, and opens well by pulling, and by pressing of the hand; and when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can well have twisting, or tear, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not possible to move the limb only by hand, but medicine is added afterward, then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And the nails which break that go into the marrow, and are two parts of the joint, it is now necessary to put them in order equally, as well as after incisions; and if after incisions the nails grow too long, if you leave them whole until the incisions are healed; then put them in order with the bone as lightly and cautiously as possible, and the nails which restore the limb are lighter than the restorations of those who have pieces; then restrain them, as is done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if it is the hand or the foot, or at the wrist if it is a small limb, or two strings, or one string and the hand; and put the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the limb that are broken are unbent, if you remember by all means the adjuncts to the bone that you must put, and keep that in your work does not cause any lesion or pain to the patient; and adjust the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if he seems that it is not well: if the wound closes well, and does not tighten too much, do not press as do some who make it come about by their work at the incision and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the limb is fixed in place, if the patient is well advised not to move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither by day nor night; and take care that the limb is so firmly secured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, if it is not at the point, and you can put it into use without pain; keep it straight, do not allow any twisting until it is restored; and the degree of recovery of the limb is as I have said.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The breaks of the limb are various in small and great size and shape.</start_of_turn
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and thighs and the like: if you can cover them with soft and subtle cloths; and those that are large, such as bones and legs: if you can cover them with a wide and strong cloth, because the large cloth embraces the whole great limb and tightens it equally from all sides, so that there is no tension; then put on firm pressure, three turns or four according to the limb, and tighten your hand one palm at the end of the break, then take away a palm from the break; and soften the cloth somewhat, as much as you can take hold of a great part of the limb, then take hold of another cloth and tighten the knot without slipping from the break; then put back to the part below the break, and tighten moderately, not too strong not too weak, as we said at the beginning of this chapter; then put between the cloths some bands of linen or cloths, until they are even, and then tie everything up with a bow, and then put your pins well made on, if there is no abscess or swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, if you put something soothing on the abscess, and which hardens the swelling, and leave it until it has gone down; then strain upon your eyes, and let them be half of a large cane resting steadily, or of a staff from which nails are made, or of reeds of palm, and let them be in this fashion.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the stick which one puts on the fracture be larger and wider than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the limb of little or great size; then strain upon the eyes just as you did at the first hour, and then bind under a thread of linen without fail, as it was at the first hour on the fracture; the tighter it is, the less; and let the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of fine linen. For if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their beds with linen thread and make a great mistake, because the thread will not be even if it is too subtle, and will not hold well.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is nauseated by the blows of the stones after the stretching of the limbs, put some sponges of linen or coarse cloth on them so that they do not bruise.</start_of_turn>
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When there is a wound with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will speak of the treatment of that later.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	The wounds that he cannot bear to endure from these stars shall break all the limbs at the first moment.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when a limb is large, it is not suitable to insert needles until after five days or seven, or more according to the severity of the wound; and when this is done, the method of ancient emblizings should be used to restore a fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some flour that adheres to the walls of a mill, mix it with eggs, and make this concoction, not too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of emblizement that restores a fracture in many situations, and even among women and young children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley and linseed and ivy and asafoetida and gum arabic and mugwort, in the amount of X; myrrh and aloes, in the amount of V; chamomile, in the amount of VII; and mix them together. If the patient’s complexion is hot, use this dressing, because it is of good composition and restores the fractured bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of emblizement that is good for torsion: take mugwort and vismut, in an X ratio; myrrh and aloes, in a VII ratio; acacia, in a VI ratio; archangels’ balsam, in an X ratio, and grind them well, mix with water or eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of supporting joints and bones are to relieve pain, reduce swelling of the bone, and break up the stiffness: take new linen, moisten it in oil and put it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plaster casts do not restore me, but they are good to soothe post-cautery pain, and bones properly the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other method of reduction that restores fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial pell leaves, and grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other methods of support are to restore the fracture of the bone and to diminish the remaining swelling
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take roots of meadowsweet, chamomile, violets flowers, wheat flour, fennel seed, one part of chamomile; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, soak with vinegar of coriander or water, and use it
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more forceful than the first, when the abscess bursts and restoration of the limb is required.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of meadowsweet, and poppy seed, balsam, melilot, and chamomile, and violet flowers and camomile, of all an equal part; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that he puts nothing on the broken limb except a little wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between two things neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen commands that we put something dry on the broken limb to restore it, such as mirre and aloes and incense and the like.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is good for wound and pain: take mugwort and chopped onions, or willow buds, and mustard, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a dressing of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen a little after, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone of its limb moved; if not loosen by hand for days. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sense rest or inflammation, if you are hasty, and loosen it, and stabilize the displacement now; and put on a light bandage, and a wet sponge of sea salt, and immerse in water, and lift the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is appeased; then leave the limb rest for an hour, and put on dry lint, moisten in water or oil rose, and bind up with a nut, until you are sure that the abscess has gone; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be sure to stabilize the pain, then repeat the binding and a little displacement, and do not strain it so much as before; and be discreet until it is healed
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see swelling, redness, pain and swelling around a bone, and if the limb returns to its original position as before, you must immediately immobilize and support it, just as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come to the limb anything of what we have said, if you must force it, do so only after three days or four, or five or seven; and in no case leave it for twenty days, as we have seen, until the bruise has disappeared, and the swelling has subsided; for in that case the restraint must be greater than before, and the limb must be padded, as I have said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than usual, the swelling will not go down; then you must apply warm water to the limb every time you move it, for every third hour, and cut a piece of licorice; by this means the swelling will be removed from the limb, and the pain will subside, just as we have experienced.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various breaks.</start_of_turn>
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures are made, of various figures, and the causes are diverse; for there are fractures which are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collarbone is fractured throughout to the syphus which is the socket of the bone, as if made by a hatchet or fist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a fracture of the hatchet.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For when the spear pierces the bone from below in a piercing fashion, and is called this kind of fracture an "absolute fracture"; and is the wound of these major or minor fractures.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fracture or break of bone, or fracture of bone on bone, or swelling on bone, or other similar things.</start_of_turn
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that approaches the joint which is below the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is closed in the bone as thinly as a cobweb, and the wound is small, and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a fracture of the cobweb; and if the wound is made or by a wound of stone, or by thorn, or by anything similar, and makes enter the piece of bone below, and the limb is limp as when making broth when they boil over the cauldron; if between the bone inwards.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this often happens under those who have or suffer from moist bones, as in children; and in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are loosened as with stars; and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all these breaks due to the detachment above them, and the inquiry of wounds, and the corrupt flesh which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The blood vessel is known by this, that when one has discovered the bone, and has wiped around it, if the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient's well-being, and if you see no other mishap, such as vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes becoming yellow and flushed, and other similar things, if it does not recover without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an impending accident, and you hope for health, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when it comes to the swelling which appears first, and which is in the armpit, if you can remove the bone before the fourteenth day from the muscle which you must remove
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day from the bone which must be removed, then the tissue of the bone will be corrupted, and there will come the accident which we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the skin that covers the brain, if you do not make an incision in the split part: and that is that you take the head of the sufferer and uncover the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more than you can; and if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or from incisions, if it is of use, and that you fill the cavity with soaked cloths in oil rose; and rest the wound until the incisions have subsided, and be sure of the evacuation of blood; then as the bone is turned to heal, and this is done in two ways: one way if the edge of the fracture is narrow in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another incision more extensive than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have a variety of different sized wounds, some wide and some narrow, and some pointed and some blunt, and on a lighter wound, do not cauterize the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, if you must pierce through, do not make the wound deeper than necessary; and must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass through the bone; and you must have several of these, so that if there is bone left in the wound of the thickness of the bone, if you have several punctures you will remove all of the bone.  This is the form of two of these punctures:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through bone is that you put on one tarer over the bone, and turn your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then you remove the tarer from another place a little later, and do the same thing all around, and cut out the space of the bone which is between the perforations, and do it more skillfully than you could, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought out the bone from your hand, or from any instrument which you have like nails, pincers; and keep your fingers away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	When the bone is pierced and treated, if it is possible, reset the loosened ligament that has come loose from the bone to some other instrument resembling a chisel, but make it more firm and flexible than the other chisel; and if nothing remains of the small bones, do not remove any scales, if the bones are slightly fractured with the instruments; then close the wound with sutures and bandages as we have said.
