Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that of the Galenicians, which is more useful; and the load is very strong, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either that which is fractured or broken open, so that when you have uncovered that part, put back the tip of this lenticular incisor, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not penetrate too deeply from one side, for the part that is towards the two costae if the puncture is towards the bone; then place a little mallet above, so that you compress the bone slightly, and take care of the cloth that is underneath; if it is against the bone, if the bone is slightly fractured, for it is well enough in its place, without excessive force or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if a bone breaks through the skin does not pierce completely, and is only slightly fractured by its underside, there are small pieces; if you can rejoin the fracture, and remove the splinters with a blunt scraper, which you must have in various quantities, to mend each limb as well as possible, according to the work and the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is before great pain, and afterwards more subtle, and does not cease to do this until it is well.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other size of capillary and fracture, it is necessary to provide the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not properly learned by anyone who has put his study into this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is discovered, take a drape of linen according to the size of the wound, and soak it in oil of roses; then place it on the wound. Take another drape of linen doubled in two or three, soak it in wine and oil of roses, and place it on the first drape. Do this more gently than you can, so as not to damage the wound. Administer further linen and do not restrain it more than is necessary to hold the wound in place; leave it in place for one or two days until the swelling subsides. Then remove it, and administer medicines such as root of hemlock, alum, and incense, and an herbalist. From these things make powder and apply it to the wound, and administer additional medicines without biting. Keep the wound clean and do not allow it to become swollen, for when it swells on the brain, it causes great harm. For when anything biting is placed on the wound, if it does not fester from beneath.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if no evil accident befalls the patient, as we have said, if there be doubt, sense be doubted.</start_of_turn>
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If darkness does not depart by the medicine which we have placed on it, and if it persists, if you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drapel, and apply it on the surface; then it shall be cured in the same manner as before, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then comes the treatment of the ways to cure it, as long as it is healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, if you must drink a little wine or broth without fail, and put the broken bone back into its natural position, and support it firmly, until it returns to its normal shape; and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the limb, and cannot come from the bone itself, then you must know that you must place the limb equal to the head of a radish.

Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind the other part once more, if the fracture is there; and let the bands be so strong that they fill the wound at the fracture.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should moisten the tents in the burn, and die each one for himself.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think it is good, but it is necessary that they be moistened in preparation of an egg and wheat flour powder; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilage is hardened.

And never do we see a hen's eggshell in place of the tentation, and if there is indeed a feather hanging, hold the brimstick, and blow the patient among them; or do as you see fit.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out while you are working, if you put some lint or cotton soaked in rose oil, or some of this vinegar.

de la routure de la mandibule	De la routure de la mandibule.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and the break is only slight, and is not broken through, except for a tooth socket, if it is known gently.

Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced, that is to say, if it is shifted, if you must administer an extension of the thumb by parts, as much as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres. Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus comes from an abscess, if it threatens what we have said many times.

de la forcele	forcefully.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful fracture occurs many times beforehand, in the shoulder, and if it is broken and dislodged in two pieces, there are fragments; and the most easy to restore. Or if there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the fracture is when the wound is toward the side, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the limb that feels the forceful fracture; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the fracture back in its place, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to stretch further, put under the shoulder of the patient a round ball of lead, or linen, and be thick as you need; and extend and hold the fracture, and strain the lead with your hand, so that you put the fracture back in its place, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you are unable to handle the head of the humerus away from its socket, because it has slipped downwards, know that the patient lies supine on his belly, and put a cushion under the shoulder, namely the middle ear, and support the shoulder blade until the bone of the humerus is elevated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture towards your side, and if you find debris, know that you must cut there; and remove the fragments gently, and if the bones cannot join together by any means, if the pulp has gone into one of the incisors that you have; but that you put a cushion under the humerus, for fear of infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it appears like a spoon, and is not at all crooked, and be as wide as it ought to be, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and have two holes, as you see, and one be large, and the other is small, as is the curvature of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of the apposition, if the wound is great, or if you doubt the apposition, if you employ the wound with bandages and stitches, according to its quantity.

Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stripping of the bone, when it is sensible to wounds and to the saw, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and egg-white, and put on light stockings, and put a pin from below the shoulder; then take a great bandage of a palm of a hand wide, then put on two layers of gauze on the stockings, and plaster; then take a splint of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage remains in place; and put the splint on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the collar, and take away the pin from below the shoulder, and the painful shoulder; and keep the chest part resting, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture in place, and you see clearly that the splint does not move from the fractured bone, if the patient has regained some sensation, and if the patient cries out, if the restraint is necessary; and make the patient rest on his back, and put under him a small cushion below the shoulder, to raise the arm up; if you align the fracture with the alignment of the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not unbind it unless there is a bad accident that does not come, until about twenty days; then repeat the plastering, if you see that there is need for it, and tighten and leave it in place, until it is restored; and it is restored in about eight days, and in less time for most people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time than any man.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder blade is broken or dislocated, do not pull it out with force; if the limb appears according to the break figure, and is restored to its natural form in all ways that you can; then put out the limb powder from the mill with abundance of eggshell, and bandage firmly, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and subtle splint, wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is not firmly fixed in any part of the shoulder, use the bundle of flaxseed, so that the splint rests evenly; and then strain it with great tension, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the mark of every joint; and every time it slackens, if you strain, and put back the splint if it has come out of its place, and leave the patient lying down; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or less. And when this number is completed, if it comes loose, and so be cured, for it is not a bone that is easily broken.

Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight is never broken in the middle, but it often breaks at the outset; but it often breaks upon exertion.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, if it inclines downwards, and causes the patient great pain, and fault of moisture, and sweat, and by chance vomiting blood, and opens the jaws in the broken bone, and they feel well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient lies prone upon his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades together, and reassemble the joints of the two ribs in your hands, and subtly force them even in all positions that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should; then place on dressings and stamp upon the external heel of the bandage with fine salt, or some softer substance, and wrap in one bandage, and bind firmly over the fracture, if it does not move; and turn the limb slowly backward, and strain gently, and reward after an hour the limb, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you fear that it will slip, due to corrosion or inflammation that comes from within, or pain or swelling, if you hurry, and it slips, remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the manner of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	And if the patient lies prone upon his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades together, and reassemble the joints of the two ribs in your hands, and subtly force them even in all positions that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should; then place on dressings and stamp upon the external heel of the bandage with fine salt, or some softer substance, and wrap in one bandage, and bind firmly over the fracture, if it does not move; and turn the limb slowly backward, and strain gently, and reward after an hour the limb, and if it relaxes, strain again; and if you fear that it will slip, due to corrosion or inflammation that comes from within, or pain or swelling, if you hurry, and it slips, remove the dressing, and address what has happened in the manner of treatment; then reapply the dressing and strain until it is healed. And in the case of a broken rib.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Its fractures of the ribs only happen at the large angles behind the back and at the head downwards; and they do not happen for anything else except that they are glassy. And one knows well at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is when you put the break back in its place, as it should be done
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the dressing, and bind it with a bandage, if you have need of it
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the fracture of the ribs has descended inwards, if the patient experiences great pain, pointing, as if of pleura, for the bone is pressing on the gut; there is vomiting and evacuation of large amounts of blood, which is a serious illness, and the former has put on great effort.</start_of_turn>
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	If any of those things mentioned above are done, it is necessary to administer food that causes the belly to swell, in order to push out the fracture.</start_of_turn>
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for the wounds that remain closed do not heal if they are not opened.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they are opened, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one puts sponges on the limb to soak up the pus, because this is almost a reason; however, there is doubt that the sponge will not pull out the pus from the limb because of the weakness of the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth soaked in oil, and put on sponges between the ribs to make the yolk equal all around; then either cure with pleurisin dressing, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points the thumb, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is possible to suture above the fractured bone, and to put in place a dressing for the support; then it must be fractured again, and treated gently, and then the two edges of the wound must be stitched together, if they are large, and it must be cured with dressing, until it is healed
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If pus comes from an abscess, put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the limb; and treat until the limb stops protruding from the abscess, and do not leave it uncovered even if necessary, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the heel, and there is doubt to the patient, if it is necessary to cut above the broken bone, and to put in a dressing; then one must pierce the bone lightly, and draw out the marrow gently, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges. And if an abscess comes up, if put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil on the wound and leave it on; and cure while the bone is being healed, as long as it is necessary. For in the bursting of the heel bone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a bursting of the bone of the heel, and often there is pain; and the same with the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to no avail, and you see that it will be healed or not, take care if you see its hands softened and limp and dead, and that they cannot be moved or extended, and when you prick them with a needle, if you do not feel it.</start_of_turn>
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The wounds that are mortal in many situations, and if you move them and feel well when you strain and prick them, the wound is saved, and the patient is cured, if you apply the remedy.</start_of_turn
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if anything similar comes to the spine, if you see that there is blood or not, if you take care that the pieces are softened, and that the accident that is in the hands or on the back is evacuated with violence and without fear; and when it has been softened on the belly, evacuate with violence and without fear.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	When it is softened on the back and it is seen to swell, it cannot be stopped.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	A wound that is mortal: if it is not treated diligently in its cure
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, if the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that if there is an abscess above, put upon the spine oil of roses or oil of nutmeg of an egg, until it is calmed; then put on one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if a bone is fractured, if you must cover over the wound; and fix the bone, then join together the two parts of the wound, if it is large, with a splint, and bandage it, then cure it with ointment until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "break of the jaw", if you have your left thumb in your pouch, and put it equal to the other hand in front, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you need them; then strain it, and if there are fractured bones, if you leave it on, and fix them, cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the thigh bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the bone of the thigh is fractured, and if there is no immediate sign of concern at the head [of the bone]; and if it lasts long, and worsens at the root, and brings pain to the patient, swelling and breaking that which is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you place your hand on the [fractured] bone, as long as you are over the fracture; and stretch out what is fractured and the shape of the limb; and if the fracture is only at the head, put it in its natural position, until it is back to its normal shape.</start_of_turn>

And if the fracture is long or it declines at the root, make the patient rest on his belly, until the restoration of this fracture is apparent.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	When you have set the hair even, if you place it on the shoulder joint, then place on a bolster of staff or crook, and hold the limb steady, so that it does not move; and keep the limb still until the hair has grown even.
